Thursday January 2 2025

Michael Marcus: Lessons from a Market Wizard

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

Let's kick off the year with some inspiration, shall we?

Ok - Michael Marcus... ever heard of him?

He's one of the original Market Wizards featured in Jack Schwager's book, and for good reason.

Marcus started his trading journey with just $30,000 and turned it into a ridiculous $80 million trading commodities.

Yes, $80 million‚Ä¶.

However you slice it, that's an incredible return.

COURAGE

Marcus sadly died in March of 2023, but left behind a ton of wisdom.

If you haven't already, I highly recommend (re)reading the first Market Wizards book to get the full picture.

But two of his quotes have always stuck with me:

  1. ‚ÄúThe best trades are the ones in which you have all three things going for you: fundamentals, technicals, and market tone.‚Äù
  2. "Being a successful trader also takes courage: the courage to try, the courage to fail, the courage to succeed, and the courage to keep going when the going gets tough."

Why These Matter

The first quote is so underrated. Even on lower timeframes, if you can align yourself with:

  • Fundamentals (higher timeframe trend)
  • Market tone (sentiment and trend persistence)
  • Technicals (trade timing and execution)

You significantly improve your odds of being right more often‚Ä¶ and securing a handsome RvR for your trouble.

The second quote? Well, it speaks for itself.

Trading is tough. Success requires the courage to step up, take risks, learn from failure, and keep going when things get hard.

A solid reminder for us all.

Cranking up the Flows for 2025

A Traders' Week Ahead Playbook

  • The Daily Fix
  • chris.weston@pepperstone.com |
  • 10:54 PM

The bull case in the USD remains

The USD Index (DXY) gained 0.8% on the week, breaking above 109, with GBP the notable underperformer in G10 FX on the week. EURUSD traded into 1.0224 but saw an element of short covering on Friday, and while all the talk remains on the timing for the spot rate to hit parity, the risk of a further squeeze higher this week looks possible. That said, I am skewed to sell rallies in EURUSD and would look to see how price reacts into 1.0345 (18 Dec low), where a more outsized rally should see rallies capped into 1.0425, which is where I'd preferably reengage with shorts.

Key data to navigate for the week ahead

Reviewing the marquee data points that could move markets this week.

US Nonfarm Payrolls (Friday 13:30 UK / Saturday 00:30 AEDT) - the median estimate is for 160k jobs to have been added in December, with the economist's estimates ranging from 200k to 120k. Subsequently, any jobs print above 200k would be considered a 'surprise', where both US 10-year yields and the USD would rise strongly. US equity would likely rally despite a rise in rates, as a strong economy should trump reduced Fed easing expectations. Conversely, a jobs outcome below 140k would work against risk and the USD. The unemployment rate is also key, and with the market eyeing an unchanged read at 4.2%, USD and equity bulls would want to see a U/E print at or below 4.2%. Conversely, a lift above 4.3% and certainly at 4.4% would likely lead to some selling of equity risk and the USD.

Monday January 6 2025

One Word for the Year

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:09 PM

A few years ago, I was listening to an (almost) billionaire talk about how he frames the new year, and it stuck with me ever since‚Ä¶

You see, we can all get lost in a list of tasks, resolutions, and goals. It's easy to get sidetracked or caught up in the chaos of life.

But here's the neat trick he used to combat that:

ONE WORD

Each year, come up with one word or short phrase that you want to represent you for the year.

Think of words or phrases like:

  • Relentless
  • Healthy
  • Beast mode
  • Aggressive
  • Family man
  • Athlete
  • Limitless
  • Bold
  • Unstoppable
  • Grateful
  • Intentional
  • Patient

Pick something that instantly conjures up the image of who you want to become in your mind.

You can then use this word or phrase as a quick reminder to align your decisions with your bigger goals.

To Dig Deeper

Let's say improving your health is your focus this year. You want to:

  • Quit some vices
  • Drop a few pounds of fat
  • Gain muscle
  • Clean up your diet
  • Run a marathon

Instead of overthinking all those goals, you could simplify everything into one word: ‚ÄúHealthy.‚Äù

That single word triggers all those smaller goals in your mind, helping you make better decisions and, over time, create a new identity.

In Trading

Your word might be:

  • Disciplined - A reminder to stick to your plan no matter what.
  • Focused - To keep your attention on what really matters.
  • Patient - if you want to slow things down.

You get the idea‚Ä¶

What would your word for 2025 be?

Tuesday January 7 2025

Playing with your VWAP

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:04 PM

I'm a fan of VWAP. So are algos and so are institutions. (I like to keep good company‚Ä¶)

The traditional VWAP is an intraday tool, a line in the sand, a fair value point that takes into account both price and volume.

Roughly speaking.

  • Price above = strong
  • Price below = weak
  • Price oscillating around the VWAP = indecision

But what about if we zoom out a bit?

Can we use the VWAP on a higher time frame to help make better trading decisions?

I think we can‚Ä¶ let's explore.

ANCHORED VWAP

On most platforms, we can 'anchor' the VWAP to a specific point, a reference point that makes sense to start the VWAP calculations from. For example:

QQQ (above): Anchored to 1st December (the first trading day of the month, a key date for many institutions). Price bounced off the anchored VWAP mid-December before Powell got involved‚Ä¶

Tesla: Anchored to the start of the month, the VWAP acted as support until it crumbled later in the year.

GBP/JPY: Anchored to the most recent swing high, providing a useful perspective.

Gold: Anchored to a recent swing low, offering a strong buy zone during its move upward.

Tip on Gold: I used the futures contract instead of the CFD for better volume precision. CFD volume is okay, but nowhere near as accurate as futures, especially on smaller timeframes.

Here's a comparison: Futures on the left, CFD on the right.

WHERE TO ANCHOR VWAP?

Anchor the VWAP to a point you believe has meaning to the market participants.

Here are some ideas:

  • Earnings releases
  • Economic data (CPI, NFP, rate decisions)
  • Major news events
  • Market open (day, week, month)
  • Breakout candles
  • Swing highs or lows
  • Key pivot levels
  • Gap start (up or down)
  • Trendline breakpoints
  • Psychological levels (e.g., $100, 4,000)
  • All-time highs or lows
  • High-volume candles
  • Previous VWAP rejection points

You get the idea.

Like everything in trading, it's all about experimenting. Try anchoring VWAP to points that resonate with your style and see how it works over time.

Happy VWAPing!

PS: I hosted a webinar called VWAP Trading Strategies which is worth a watch if you're into VWAP.

When fishermen can't go to sea.

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:09 PM

I'm not sure why this popped up on my X timeline, I don't follow the guy.

But sometimes, the message is just oh-so-perfect for us traders‚Ä¶

EVEN IN STILLNESS, THERE'S PROGRESS

For traders, this means that when there's no opportunity, when the market isn't setting up, it's time to change gears.

Take that time to read, reflect, study and journal.

Because trying to trade in a choppy market environment is like fishing in a storm. Sure, you might get lucky‚Ä¶ but there's a good chance you'll just wipe out.

It's better to step back and use the downtime wisely:

  • Pick up that trading book gathering dust on your shelf.
  • Watch that webinar you bookmarked months ago.
  • Dive into your journal and analyse past trades.

Progress doesn't always mean action, it can come from preparation, reflection, and learning.

Thursday January 9 2025

How to Know When You're Ready to Size Up

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

Ah sizing up‚Ä¶ something on the mind of most traders.

‚ÄúHow do I get bigger and make more from my trades?‚Äù

But before you take that leap, ask yourself this:

‚ÄúWhy do I want to size up?‚Äù

Now, this might sound like a stupid question. You're probably thinking, ‚ÄúTo make more money, obviously, Mark. Duh‚Äù

Sure‚Ä¶but if that's the objective, there are other things you could do first.

SIZING UP

As soon as you increase size, you increase risk. There's no getting around it. Double the size, double the risk.

And here's where many traders stumble, they start trading differently, using tighter stops or second-guessing their setups because they're uncomfortable with the larger position.

So, before you jump to sizing up, consider these steps first:

  1. Reduce your losers.

    2. If you can eliminate unnecessary losing trades, you'll boost your bottom line without taking on more risk.

  2. Hold your winners longer.

    3. If your strategy allows for it, extend your holding time on strong trades. Why take on the risk of a new trade when the one you're already in is working perfectly well?

Exhaust these options first.

Squeeze every drop of profit from your winners (within reason, we live in the real world here, it will never be perfect) and cut the dumb mistakes. That alone is a significant boost to your P&L.

READY TO SIZE UP?

Let's assume you've optimised your trading, now what?

Before you size up, make sure:

  • Your discipline is bulletproof.

    • Any cracks in your discipline will be magnified by larger size.

  • You're consistent.

    • Erratic returns and sizing up don't mix. Murphy's Law almost guarantees you'll size up right before a drawdown!

  • You've handled drawdowns before.

    • Have you proven you can stick to your process through a rough patch? If not, hold off.

Be brutally honest:

Are you sizing up because you're frustrated with slow progress, or is it a calculated decision to scale up a system that's been working consistently over time?

When the time is right, you'll know‚Ä¶ you'll feel like you've earned the right to trade bigger. At that point, you can create a solid plan of action to increase size with confidence.

DISCIPLINE

📺Why Most Traders Lose: Jason Shapiro on Disciplined Trading

Here are the key takeaways:

    2. This must align with your trade idea, don't just wing it.

The UK (and perhaps the US) in the corner losing the bond market

  • The Daily Fix |
  • chris.weston@pepperstone.com |
  • 12:22 AM

A playbook for US nonfarm payrolls - Do all road lead to US equity weakness?

Making a call on how US Treasuries and the USD react is fairly straightforward - if the U/E rate remains unchanged at 4.2%, and we see the number of payrolls come in above 200k+ then we will likely see Treasury yields rise and the USD finding good buyers. However, given we saw US equity sold in reaction to this week's hotter ISM Services and JOLTS print, the possible reaction in US equity to a better NFP print is now less clear - in theory, a solid NFP outcome should lift stocks, but with concerns of rising term premium, a higher discount rate and an early rise in inflation expectations, we could feasibly see a re-run of the ISM services move.

That being good data resulting in sellers of equity risk. Clearly, the US Treasury market holds the answers.

Conversely, a scenario where we see a weaker-than-expected NFP print (say below 130k), with a rise in the U/E rate would typically result in Treasury yields, the USD and equity all moving lower. I suspect this will also be the case this time around, and equity will unlikely rally just because Treasury yields are falling.

So, does this mean all roads from the NFP print lead to sellers in US equity? It seems that most paths do take us towards that outcome, and we'd need to see an outcome that is almost perfectly aligned to consensus expectations - not too hot, not too cold - and one that limits the movement in 10- and 30-year Treasuries.

Navigating Increasingly Choppy Waters

A Traders' Week Ahead Playbook

  • The Daily Fix
  • chris.weston@pepperstone.com |
  • 9:57 PM

US CPI is the marquee data risk this week

Recall the median estimate in the Fed's recent Statement of Economic Projection (SEP) was for core PCE inflation to come in at 2.8% in December - so should the elements from this week's US PPI and CPI reports feed into a higher implied core PCE tracking rate (due on 31 January), then the Fed's median 2.8% estimate would likely be seen as lowball and would justify the central pricing for just one rate cut this year - in fact, we may even start to hear increased talk of rate hike risk later this year - a point where the contrarian in me would feel Treasuries become a tactical buy and to position for increased rate cuts to start to be re-priced.

What can derail the USD rally?

DXY (blue) vs US 10yr real Treasury

The rise in US real rates and the repricing of the US interest rate swaps curve has been a clear tailwind for the USD, and the greenback is undoubtedly finding love from all circles within the FX ecosystem. On Friday we saw technical USD bullish breakouts vs the CHF, SEK, AUD, GBP, and NZD. That said, the downside in EURUSD still needs work to convince and requires a concerted push below the prior lows of 1.0224. USDCAD needs the buyers to step up for a push above the range highs of 1.4450, but I'd be looking for that to materialise should we see a hotter US core CPI print.

Many question what stops the USD from climbing further higher, however, the reality is that on current trends, we look around the G10 currency region and see a scarcity of attractive alternatives. The USD offers carry, relative growth, a hedge from looming tariff risk, and importantly it has momentum and trend working in its favour.

What derails the USD bull trend structurally would be improved economic data from other nations, and/or the upcoming US growth and inflation data starting to crack and deteriorate - a seemingly low risk at this point, but it is feasible from late Q125. Tactically, the near-term risk for USD longs - other than a below consensus US core CPI and retail sales print - is positioning, with the USD now well-owned by real money accounts, and to a lesser extent leveraged players.

Monday January 13 2025

Lose the Battle, Win the War

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:11 PM

Imagine this:

You're an Army General, in charge of multiple regiments, anywhere from 10,000 to 1,000,000+ soldiers.

Your mission? Deploy those soldiers in the most effective way on the battlefield. In a perfect world, there would be no casualties‚Äîbut this is war, and casualties are inevitable.

An experienced General aims to minimise losses while focusing on the ultimate goal: winning the war.

LOSE THE BATTLE, WIN THE WAR

Now picture this:

The General is overseeing a battle, a battle that's being lost. The enemy holds the high ground, superior weapons, and better tactics.

The General has two options:

  1. Keep fighting - Knowing the chances of heavy losses are high.
  2. Withdraw - Preserve men and resources to regroup and fight another day.

The most rational choice? Withdraw. Live to fight another day.

Now flip the script and view this through the lens of trading.

You are the General, and your capital is your army. Each trade is a battle you aim to win.

But as a pragmatic trader, you understand you can't win them all. Your job is to preserve your resources and deploy them only when you have the advantage.

  • Wait for the great setups. Trades with edge, where the odds are in your favour.
  • Recognise when the battle is lost. If you're taking loss after loss, accept that today's battle isn't yours to win. Stop trading, take the loss, and regroup.

The Big Picture

You can lose many battles and still win the war.

In trading terms: you can endure losing trades or even losing days and still have an exceptional year.

It's all about playing the long game and preserving your resources for when it really matters.

US PPI leads us into the CPI report

Today's US core PPI inflation data is expected to rise 0.3% m/m / 3.8% y/y (from 3.4%). This is an important data point, in that analysts will take various components from the PPI calculation and feed them into their models to gain a sense of the tracking rate for US core PCE inflation (due 31 Jan) - an outcome in PPI that therefore misses/beats expectations by a margin does have the potential to move US Treasuries around and by extension the USD, equity and crypto too.

With a number of big US banks reporting tomorrow, we've seen better buying interest in the big money centres, but most seem to be running a more neutral position into earnings. The XLF ETF has regained a footing above the 100-day MA, which is a small positive, while JP Morgan is testing the top of its recent tight consolidation range and is worth putting on the radar, as an upside break of $245.69 post earnings (JPM report in the pre-market session tomorrow) may be worth chasing.

Non-Negotiable Mistakes

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

Some mistakes are simply not acceptable‚Ä¶

They have serious consequences.

  • ‚ÄúOh, I forgot to wait at the junction and just drove out‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúOops, I didn't look before walking across the road‚Äù

Too many of those and you're brown bread!

Compare that to something minor, forgetting to close a window or leaving your phone in the car.

Sure, life would be better without those mistakes, but they aren't going to kill you. The same applies to trading‚Ä¶

NOT ACCEPTABLE

There are some mistakes that you should not be making.

  • Breaking daily risk rules
  • Oversizing on positions

These are the trading equivalent of stepping into traffic without looking, mistakes that could be account-ending.

On the other hand, there are smaller mistakes:

  • Entering a trade slightly late.
  • Closing a trade too early.

They might frustrate you, but they won't wipe you out. You want to reduce them over time of course, but it's not life and death‚Ä¶

In my latest podcast, I dive deeper into this topic, breaking down the difference between non-negotiable mistakes and those that are simply part of the learning curve.

There's a common misconception that great traders make no mistakes, and that's simply not true.

Even the best traders make errors all the time, the difference is their mistakes are rarely life-threatening. (Unless you're Nick Leeson‚Ä¶)

Check out the episode here. 🎧Non-Negotiable Mistakes: The Fine Line Between Growth and Failure

Wednesday January 15 2025

The One Trading Skill That Changes Everything

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

Here's a Chinese proverb that is so on point for traders:

"One moment of patience may ward off great disaster. One moment of impatience may ruin a whole life."

Let's talk about that moment of impatience‚Ä¶ the one where you pull the trigger too soon, chase a setup that doesn't fit your plan, or double down on a loss out of frustration.

We've all been there. And we all know how it ends.

SUPERPOWER

In trading, patience is more than just waiting.

It's about waiting with intention‚Ä¶ for your edge, for confirmation, and for the right conditions.

Here's how to turn patience into your trading superpower:

  1. Wait for Your Setup

    2. Not every price move deserves your attention. Focus only on trades that align with your edge, and let everything else go.

  2. Accept That Missed Trades Happen

    3. It's way better to miss an opportunity than to jump into a bad trade. There will always be another setup.

  3. Use a Checklist Before Entering

    4. Train yourself to pause. Run through a quick checklist before entering any trade.

    Ask:

    • Does this align with my strategy?
    • Is my stop and target clear?
    • Am I trading my plan or my emotions?
  4. Practice the Art of Sitting on Hands

    5. On slow days, resist the urge to ‚Äúforce it.‚Äù Those small, unnecessary trades can quickly add up to big losses.

The Bigger Picture

Every great trader I know preaches patience:

  • Patience to wait for the setup.
  • Patience to let your winners run.
  • Patience to manage losses and preserve capital.
  • Patience to trade the process month after month after month

The market rewards discipline over impulsiveness.

Every. Single. Time.

Remember, one moment of patience today can protect your account, and your mindset, for the long haul.

So, next time you feel the urge to trade impulsively, pause.

Take a breath. Remind yourself of the long game.

Thursday January 16 2025

The Timeless Art of Reading the Tape

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

In my early trading years (2001+), I dedicated all my time to reading the tape.

I was glued to the order book, time and sales, and a 1-minute chart, learning to spot early algos and iceberg orders, then trading around them.

Back then, algos were so primitive that if you identified one at work, you could assume there was more size behind it. You'd bid one tick above and use it as a wall of support.

There were plenty of plays.

But as the market evolved and algos became smarter, that game ended. Orders became harder to spot as they worked more discreetly, letting price drop, sweeping offers, and mixing it up to avoid detection.

Fast forward to today, and the game has completely changed.

Yet one thing remains constant: price and how it moves.

TAPE READING: THEN AND NOW

If you've read Reminiscences of a Stock Operator, you'll know Jesse Livermore used to read the tape.

Back in the 1930s, traders watched prices come through a ticker tape machine, gauging market strength or weakness based on price changes.

For example:

  • 70,71,73,75,77,81,81,83,84 = Strong tape, urgent buying
  • 70,71,72,71,72,71,71,70,71 = Mixed, no urgency

They focused on:

  • Pace of the tape
  • Price changes
  • Price response to key levels

These insights helped them anticipate where the market might go next.

TODAY'S TAPE

Sure, we aren't reading prices on thin strips of paper anymore, but the principles are the same.

Ask yourself:

  • How does price respond to a prior high or low?
  • What's the speed of price change?
  • How much volume and range occurred in that 5-minute window?
  • Is there urgency in the price action at the open?

By observing how price reacts at key levels and critical moments, you can uncover who's in control, and use that insight to inform your trades.

These days, I believe that's enough edge without needing Level 2 or the Order Book. (Though if watching the ladder works for you, keep going!)

We've almost done a full circle. Watching price only, then watching price and market depth, now back to watching price whilst the robots battle it out on the book‚Ä¶

The tape may have evolved, but price still tells a story.

Friday January 17 2025

It's Supposed to Be Hard‚Ä¶

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:06 PM

In a recent interview, Jensen Huang, the CEO of Nvidia, said:

‚ÄúBuilding a company and building Nvidia turned out to have been a million times harder than I expected it to be, than any of us expected it to be.‚Äù

‚ÄúPersistence and resilience are key to overcoming challenges and achieving success.‚Äù

Sure, we're not building one of the world's biggest companies, but trading is no walk in the park.

It's exhausting, mentally draining, and in the early days often feels like a pointless battle.

But here's the truth, it's supposed to be that way‚Ä¶

THE TOUGH JOURNEY

The game is tough because the rewards are directly proportional to the effort involved.

Build a Streak, Master Discipline

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

Here's a neat little discipline hack for you.

This one came from trader Ruchir, listen to my conversation with him here:

🎧 From 9-to-5 to All-In: Ruchir Patel's Leap to Full-Time Trading

Now, Ruchir picked it up from somewhere else‚Ä¶ so whoever originally came up with it, credit where it's due.

It's a simple, effective way to level up your discipline‚Ä¶

STREAKS

The idea is to gamify your trading discipline.

Here's how it works:

  1. Set Clear Rules

    2. Create a small set of rules that are straightforward, with clear yes/no answers. No ambiguity or subjective interpretations.

    Examples:
    • Good Rule: Did I stick to my max 5 trades per day rule?
    • Flakey Rule: Did I trade well?
  2. Track Daily

    3. Each day, check if you followed all your rules. If yes, you earn 1 streak mark.

    • Day 1 = 1
    • Day 2 = 2
    • Day 6 = 6

    But‚Ä¶ if you break a rule, your streak resets to zero.

    You get the idea‚Ä¶

  3. Build Momentum

    4. As your streak grows, you'll be more motivated to stick to your rules, you won't want to break the streak.

    Rinse and repeat until you are a disciplined wizard!

    Oh and actually, the Traders Mastermind Discipline Tracker Google Sheet is perfect for this. With a bit of tweaking, you can set up a streak system and start building momentum.

    If you don't already have it, download it free here and watch the explainer video.

    ⭳ Get Your Discipline Tracker Now - Download, Watch, and Start Today

Turn discipline into a game, and watch how quickly your consistency improves.

Sh1t was rough.

Fast forward to today, and many of the Stoics' principles and virtues still apply, especially to trading‚Ä¶

STOIC VIRTUES

The Stoics believed in four key virtues:

  1. Wisdom

    2. The ability to make sound judgments, think rationally, and act based on knowledge and understanding.

  2. Courage

    3. The strength to face challenges, endure adversity, and take action even when it's difficult.

  3. Justice

    4. Acting fairly, ethically, and with integrity, treating others with respect.

  4. Temperance

    5. Practicing self-control, moderation, and restraint, avoiding excess or overindulgence.

The parallels to trading are obvious, right?

I believe a great trader embodies these virtues not just in the markets but in life.

Improving bit by bit as a person often brings the added bonus of becoming a better trader‚Ä¶ and vice versa.

Something to ponder‚Ä¶

Remember when you first started trading?

You were buzzing with excitement, eager to dive in. Playing with the trading platform, learning about charts and indicators, figuring out risk-to-reward ratios‚Ä¶

It felt like you'd discovered a cheat code.

What's not to love? Sitting at your screens, predicting price movements in the financial markets.

But then reality hit:

  • ‚ÄúThis damn game is tougher than I thought!‚Äù

Still, you stuck with it. You knew it wasn't going to be easy, but you didn't quit. You took on the challenge.

And then came the next step‚Ä¶

VALLEY OF DESPAIR

This is where things get really tricky.

Everywhere you turn feels like a dead end. Your strategy doesn't work. Nothing sticks.

Welcome to the Valley of Despair. (Sounds like a lovely holiday destination, doesn't it‚Ä¶)

It's here that many traders start strategy-hopping:

  • ‚ÄúMaybe I'll have better luck with DAX instead of FX.‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúMaybe this new indicator will change everything.‚Äù

And so the cycle repeats‚Ä¶ giddy excitement, harsh reality, back into the valley.

(Doom and gloom so far, I know. But stay with me.)

If you can hold on, if you can resist the urge to quit or keep chasing shiny objects, eventually, you'll claw your way out.

And that's when you'll reach the next stage: Informed Optimism.

At this stage you know what needs to be done, you can see light at the end of the tunnel and are pretty bullish on the future‚Ä¶ it just takes time.

The next step? Achievement.

This is where the rubber finally meets the road.

You start seeing the payoff from all those hours of work. The strategy tweaks, the mindset shifts, the discipline‚Ä¶ it all begins to click.

SO, WHERE ARE YOU?

Every trader goes through these stages.

Turn ChatGPT Into Your Trading Accountability Buddy

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:05 PM

Still waiting for the AI robot that can clean the house, wash the car, and take the bins out?

Yeah, me too...

But until that glorious day arrives, let's work with what we do have‚ÄîChatGPT.

It might not buff your car to a mirror shine just yet, but it can be a time-saving trading assistant.

Here's how...

YOUR AI TRADING ACCOUNTABILITY BUDDY

If there's one way ChatGPT can really help, it's by maintaining a consistent trading process and keeping your discipline on point.

The idea?

Create your very own Trading Accountability Buddy.

Here's how it works:

  • Tell ChatGPT:
  • "I want you to act as my trading accountability buddy. Each morning, ask me these pre-market questions one by one and challenge my answers to ensure I've thought them through properly.‚Äù

Then paste in your pre-market checklist, like this:

Market Conditions
  • Have you checked the overnight news and global markets?
  • What's the pre-market trend for the S&P 500, NASDAQ, or Dow?
  • Are there any major economic reports or events scheduled today?
Watchlist
  • Have you updated your watchlist for the day?
  • Are there any stocks gapping up or down significantly in pre-market?
  • What are the key levels (support/resistance) for your top 3 tickers?
Trading Plan
  • What setups are you looking for today (trend continuation, reversals, etc.)?
  • What are your planned entries, stop-losses, and targets for each trade?
  • Do you have alternative scenarios if the market doesn't behave as expected?
Risk Management
  • What is your max risk per trade and for the day?
  • Have you double-checked your position sizing calculations?
  • Is there a plan to avoid overtrading if conditions aren't favourable?
Mental Prep
  • How are you feeling today? (Stressed, focused, tired?)
  • Do you have a plan to stay disciplined and avoid impulsive trades?
  • Have you reviewed yesterday's trades to learn from them?

Here's what happens:

  1. ChatGPT will ask you each question individually, waiting for your response.
  2. It'll challenge your answers to ensure you've considered them thoroughly.
  3. Once done, it can summarise your answers and even highlight areas to improve.

For example, when asked about market conditions, ChatGPT might say:

  • ‚ÄúHave you checked global markets thoroughly? What about any major earnings or Fed speeches today?‚Äù

And then it moves to the next question.

You get the idea‚Ä¶

BONUS TIP

You can go even further by asking ChatGPT to fetch data for you, like economic calendars or earnings reports, to streamline your prep.

TRY IT OUT

If you don't already have a ChatGPT account, grab one at OpenAI and start experimenting. I use the paid version which is $20pm or something, but they do have a free version.

It's not a magic bullet, but I think it's an excellent tool to stay sharp, organised, and disciplined.

The 5-Day Discipline Challenge

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:08 PM

Discipline is the cornerstone of success‚Ä¶

Yeah yeah.

‚ÄúMark, I know this! But I still struggle‚Ä¶gimme something tactical‚Äù

Alright, I hear you. Let's break it down into baby steps.

How about a 5-day challenge?

(Time to tap into that competitive streak I know you've got.)

Here's the plan‚Ä¶

THE 5-DAY DISCIPLINE CHALLENGE

For the next five days, stick to one simple rule:

  • Start each trading day with a list of 3 things you'll do, no matter what.
  • That's it.
  • Not 2, not 5, not 20‚Ä¶ just 3.

Here's how it works:

  1. Pick 3 high-impact actions every morning.
    2. Examples:
    • Run through your pre-market checklist.
    • Set clear entry, exit, and risk levels before each trade.
    • Take a 5-minute break after every trade to review your execution.
  2. Stick to them. No exceptions.

    3. If it's on your list, it gets done. No excuses. No ‚ÄúI'll do it later.‚Äù

  3. Review your results every evening.

    4. Did you follow through? Where did you slip up? What will you adjust tomorrow?

Why does this work?

Because trading success isn't about big wins or complex strategies. It's about mastering small, repeatable habits that build discipline over time.

Build discipline, build confidence.

So, here's your Day 1 task:

  • Write down 3 non-negotiable actions you'll take today.
  • Keep them simple. Keep them specific. Then, execute.

Most traders won't even make it past Day 3. But if you commit to the full 5 days, you'll notice something:

You're calmer. More focused. More in control.

That's the power of discipline.

Give it a go‚Ä¶ you can do 5 days? Right?

Thursday January 30 2025

Stochastics + ADR = Scalpers Dream?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:01 PM

If you're one of those traders who rolls their eyes at indicators, I feel you, and I know you're about a millisecond away from hitting delete‚Ä¶ but stick with me for a second.

This might just spark a fresh idea for a discretionary scalping approach or even a testable rule-based system‚Ä¶

(And, as always, this isn't advice, do your own research. I'm just sharing something I found interesting. Cool? Cool.)

So, here's the setup: Last week, while watching Trump's speech at Davos, I noticed the usual market chaos:

  • Order books thinned out.
  • Nasdaq spiked up and down as traders reacted.
  • And once he stopped talking, it was back to normal price behaviour.

Why? Institutions and market makers pull liquidity to avoid getting caught off guard by anything unpredictable.

That leaves the book thinner than usual, so when size hits the bid or offer, it creates exaggerated price spikes.

And as a scalper, those whipsaws could be gold.

Here's where a blend of two indicators comes in‚Ä¶

STOCHASTICS + ADR

Now, I'm not usually a fan of stochastics‚Ä¶ but ADR? I like it.

Here's the concept:

  • Stochastics helps identify when price is at the upper or lower range of its recent movement.
  • ADR (Average Daily Range) highlights abnormal spikes in price activity compared to the norm. (Especially when you compare two lookbacks.)

Combine the two, and you've got a simple way to spot potential opportunities:

Example Strategy:

  1. Use a 10-second chart (yes, tiny timeframe, it's scalping).
    2. For a long trade:
    • Stochastics shows oversold.
    • ADR(1) > ADR(20) (the current bar's range is larger than the average of the last 20 bars = price spike).
    For a short trade:
    • Stochastics shows overbought.
    • ADR(1) > ADR(20).

    Keep it simple with a stop and target of 1 ADR.

    Here's what a chart looked like after modifying our premium Amber indicator to visualise this:

    📜 TM Scalper (Amber)

FINAL THOUGHTS

So, the chart's quite interesting‚Ä¶ but let's be honest it's a small sample size (1 speech!) and there's lots of work to do to turn it into a robust risk-managed system.

But, it could be a decent seed of an idea. (Many one for you scalpers and system designers‚Ä¶)

If you take this idea further and turn it into something actionable, I'd love to hear how it plays out.

For now, just sharing my experiments.

A Japanese Saying Every Trader Needs to Hear

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:02 PM

Another week of trading wrapped up.

I love the markets and trading, but there's something about the weekends...

A chance to reflect, reset, and recharge without all the noise in preparation to go again on Monday. (I don't know how you Crypto boys and girls can stay on point 24/7!)

If you get a chance to unwind in preparation for another busy trading week ahead, think about this‚Ä¶

DIRECTION NOT SPEED

Focus on direction, not speed.

I came across this post from Sahil Bloom on X recently, and while he probably wasn't talking about trading‚Ä¶ it's so relevant to us.

How often do you catch yourself rushing the process? Chasing that equity curve goal as fast as possible, without really considering the path you're on‚Ä¶

Ask yourself:

  • Is this strategy truly aligned with where I want to go?
  • Is my discipline solid, or am I just getting lucky and hoping?

It's far better to slow down, audit where you're heading, and make any necessary course corrections.

Running at full speed in the wrong direction only gets you further from where you want to be.

I also stumbled across this Japanese saying:

  • ‚ÄúIf you get on the wrong train, get off at the nearest station. The longer it takes to get off, the more expensive the return trip will be.‚Äù

It's spot on for trading.

If something doesn't feel right, whether it's your strategy, mindset, or process, don't just ‚Äústick it out‚Äù for the sake of it.

Make the adjustments now.

Use those resources - time, focus, and energy to steer toward the right destination for you.

DeepSeek vs. NVDA: The Market's Distracted, Are You?

  • Traders Mastermind |

So, last week was pretty spicy - DeepSeek put stocks like NVDA into DeepSh1t (Alright alright, I'll get my coat‚Ä¶)

But the thing is, unless trading these headline events is part of your process it's all just a distraction.

All the analysts, talking heads, and papers are covering the story.

  • üìâ ‚ÄúDeepSeek sparks AI selloff‚Äù
  • üí∞ ‚ÄúRecord market cap loss for Nvidia‚Äù
  • ü§ñ ‚ÄúDeepSeek raises questions over AI-related capex‚Äù

Rah rah rah.

And yeah, it's a big deal. AI is the investment driver right now, so sure, it's making headlines.

But does it actually matter to you and your trading?

STAY FOCUSED

If you're day trading EUR/USD or position trading Crude, none of this matters.

Heck, even if you're trading the NASDAQ, which took a hit, the news itself doesn't matter. It's out, it's priced in, and the market is reacting.

What does matter?

  • Your process.
  • What price action is telling you.
  • Whether your setup is there.
  • How your filters look.
  • Where your next trade trigger is.
  • How well you're managing your discipline.

I call times like these Max Noise Events‚Ä¶ when the entire trading world is fixated on the same thing, debating who's right and who's wrong.

They happen every so often, and do you know what our job is?

  • Understand it.
  • Acknowledge its impact on price.
  • Smile, nod‚Ä¶ then switch off the noise and get back to work.

Your edge still comes from execution, discipline, and risk management, probably not from playing the guessing game.

  • Traders Mastermind |

‚ÄúI always define my risk, and I don't have to worry about it.‚Äù

Almost like saying, ‚ÄúKnow where your stop is before you take a trade‚Äù

Common sense. Level 1 trading.

But‚Ä¶there's more to it than meets the eye.

PEACE

Most traders think risk management is just about protecting capital. But what if it's also about protecting your mind?

Think about it right, how much stress, anxiety, and frustration in trading comes from uncertainty?

  • The ‚Äúshould I hold or cut?‚Äù panic‚Ä¶
  • The ‚ÄúI'll just move my stop a bit‚Äù excuse‚Ä¶

PTJ? He doesn't deal with that.

Before he even clicks buy, he already knows his exit, if it works, great. If it doesn't, no problem. He's out.

No emotional drain. No second-guessing. No stress.

That's real peace in trading.

And when your mind is clear, you make better trading decisions.

Most traders think they want more winning trades‚Ä¶

But what they really need is more mental clarity.

Define your risk. Find peace.

Thursday, February 6 2025

The Biggest Trading Feud Ever

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:03 PM

Let's talk about Bill Ackman.

Founder and CEO of Pershing Square Capital, with a net worth of approximately $10 billion, he's pretty much nailed the hedge fund game.

But even the best aren't immune to mistakes‚Ä¶ and Ackman's infamous Herbalife short trade is proof of that.

Let's break it down, learn from his mistakes, and most importantly recognise that even the best in the world get it wrong sometimes‚Ä¶ (so no need to beat yourself up over that missed fill.)

THE HERBALIFE SHORT TRADE

In 2013, an analyst from Pershing Square pitched Ackman the idea of shorting Herbalife, a company selling dietary supplements, like shakes, bars, and the like through multi-level marketing (MLM).

For context, MLM involves individuals selling products while recruiting others to do the same, earning commissions from both their own sales and their recruits.

Here's how it works: I buy a batch of shakes at wholesale, sell a few tubs to you, and then recruit you to do the same with your friends. You sell a few, sign up some of your pals, and they repeat the process with their own circles.

The cycle keeps going, relying on a steady stream of new recruits to keep the money flowing.

It's not illegal, but it can sometimes push boundaries, depending on how the structure is set up.

Anyway, back to the trade‚Ä¶ Ackman alleged that Herbalife:

  • Made misleading claims.
  • Operated an unsustainable business model.
  • Preyed on vulnerable communities.

So, he publicly announced a large short position, backed by research, hoping media attention would enhance his trade.

And at first, it worked‚Ä¶ The stock dropped, and Ackman looked like a genius.

Enter Carl Icahn.

Years earlier, Ackman had made an enemy of Icahn, another billionaire fund manager with a reputation for aggressive tactics.

Smelling an opportunity for revenge, Icahn built a massive long position in Herbalife and publicly mocked Ackman's short.

The beef escalated when the two faced off live on CNBC, trading insults and calling each other names like schoolboys on national television.

Watch the clip on YouTube, it's surreal!:

📺 Billionaire Brawl: Icahn vs. Ackman | CNBC

In the end, Ackman's position dragged on for years, and he eventually had to cut the trade, walking away with over $1 billion in losses.

ACKMAN'S MISTAKES

Ackman later reflected on what went wrong:

  1. Naked Shorting

    He typically used Credit Default Swaps to limit his downside, but here he shorted the stock directly, exposing himself to unlimited losses. (was this his biggest mistake?)

  2. Emotional Involvement

    Once Icahn got involved, it became personal‚Ä¶ a battle of egos rather than a trade idea. (TBF Icahn played a blinder here, he knew how to turn the screw)

  3. Blinded by Bias

    Ackman became so emotionally invested that he couldn't see the trade clearly. He was convinced Herbalife should fail and refused to consider he might be wrong or that the trade was mistimed. Despite being proven right eventually, poor timing and emotions turned this bad boy into a costly mistake.

(Check out Ackman's full breakdown of the trade in this Lex Fridman interview. It's worth a watch.)

📺Bill Ackman explains Herbalife saga and beef with Carl Icahn | Lex Fridman Podcast Clips

LESSONS FOR US TRADERS

Even after losing a billion dollars, after clearing the decks Ackman bounced back, posting a 58% return in 2019 and an astounding 70% in 2020. So, what can we learn from this?

  1. The best make mistakes.

    Even seasoned pros aren't immune to breaking rules and making bad trades, accept it and move on.

  2. Control your emotions.

    When emotions rule, logic fails.

  3. Stick to your golden rules.

    Ackman broke his own rule by shorting stock directly. If he hadn't, the trade might have ended differently.

  4. Don't get married to a position.

    When the thesis changes, so should you.

  5. Clear the slate.

    Sometimes, closing out everything and starting fresh is the best move.

  6. Trust your process.

    Your strategy exists for a reason‚Ä¶ don't abandon it.

And while none of us will likely lose a billion dollars on a trade (yet‚Ä¶ I know there are some pretty ambitious traders reading this, give them a decade or so), the principles remain the same, no matter your account size.

Trade smart, stay disciplined, and remember: mistakes are part of the journey‚Ä¶ but only if you learn from them.

PS: Yes, I know this is longer than usual, I just thought it was a cool story‚Ä¶ normal service resumes tomorrow :-)

Most Traders Ask the Wrong Questions ‚Äî Are You One of Them?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

There's a simple shift that can change your entire trading game‚Ä¶

  • It's not a new strategy.
  • It's not an indicator.
  • It's not even about psychology (well, maybe‚Ä¶)

It's about asking better questions‚Ä¶

ASK BETTER QUESTIONS

See, most traders ask the wrong ones. (Guilty as charged‚Ä¶ this was me 20 years ago as a developing trader üôãüèº‚Äç‚ôÇÔ∏è)

  • ❌ Why does this always happen to me?
  • ❌ Why can't I be more disciplined?
  • ❌ Why do I keep missing trades?

These are dead-end questions. They lead to frustration, excuses, and no real progress.

Great traders ask:

  • ✅ What can I learn from this losing spell?
  • ✅ How can I improve my execution by just 1%?
  • ✅ What's stopping me from following my plan, and how do I fix it?

Exactly the same situation‚Ä¶ but a different lens.

One keeps you stuck. The other moves you forward.

So here's your challenge for today:

Before your next trade, before your next review‚Ä¶ ask yourself a better question.

  • Your default will be whatever you've always asked.
  • But pause. Reframe.
  • Push for a better answer.

It's a skill worth mastering.

📜Training Traders: The Role of Simulation in Supercharging Learning

MARKET REPLAY: AN UNDERRATED EDGE

A lot of traders I know use the replay function on TradingView.

But I'd bet more don't than do‚Ä¶ and I think that's a missed opportunity.

Here's how a simulator can level up your game:

  • üîÑ Replay your own trades: Both the ones you nailed and the ones you butchered. Missing a trade by a few ticks stings‚Ä¶ but you can replay and see what you missed
  • ‚è≥ Replay key times of day: Like every opening 15 minutes from the last month, compressed into a weekend. Mainlining opens on a Sunday morning, anyone?!

The list is endless.

So this weekend, maybe take a minute to think:

How could you use simulation to refine your execution and price action read?

Press Your Edge or Walk Away? The Trader's Dilemma

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:01 PM

So, you're up big on the day‚Ä¶ now what?

Do you keep trading, pressing your edge? Or do you lock in those gains before you give it all back?

LOCK OR NOT

There are two schools of thought here‚Ä¶

Option 1: Press Your Edge

If you're in tune with the market and firing on all cylinders, so why stop?

Opportunities aren't evenly distributed across the week, month, or quarter.

When conditions are right, you press your advantage‚Ä¶ because who knows when the next prime market rhythm will come?

Option 2: Lock It In & Walk Away

Taking profits when you're up big protects your P&L and your mindset.

Because nothing feels worse than going from king of the market to questioning your entire existence in a matter of hours‚Ä¶ (hands up please!)

And the psychological damage of giving back gains? Brutal. Sometimes, it's just not worth the risk for a little extra.

So‚Ä¶ which is right?!

Well‚Ä¶ in true trading fashion. It depends.

  • Where are you in your trading journey?

Huh? Why does that matter, Mark?

Because sometimes, protecting confidence is more important than squeezing out extra gains.

If you're still building your confidence bank, the risk vs. reward of making a little more versus giving back your gains probably isn't worth it.

But if you're more advanced and comfortable with the trade-off? Maybe pressing harder is the right move.

It's a very personal decision.

Let's Figure This Out‚Ä¶

In my latest podcast, I break down this dilemma and some smart ways to handle it.

Here's what we cover:

  • The psychology of giving back profits (and how to avoid the emotional spiral)
  • Smart ways to set intraday loss limits, without trading scared
  • When to keep your foot on the throttle (and when to step off)
  • The one mindset shift that keeps your equity curve moving in the right direction

Because let's be honest‚Ä¶ nothing stings more than being up big, feeling on top of the world, only to give it all back by the close.

If that's ever happened to you (or keeps happening), this is worth a listen.

🎧 Lock In Profits or Keep Trading? How to Avoid Giving Back Gains

How to Turn Any Trading Video Into an Actionable Plan with AI

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:07 PM

Ever watched a trading video, thought ‚ÄúThat's gold‚Äù‚Ä¶ and then completely forgot to apply it?

Or maybe you saved a good video, knowing it's probably packed with value, but never got around to watching it?

We've all been there‚Ä¶

Most traders watch YouTube, nod along, and then‚Ä¶ nothing changes. They know what to do but don't actually do it.

There's a better way:

  • Find a solid video from someone you respect
  • Grab the transcript (YouTube auto-generates captions‚Äîjust copy & paste)
  • Use ChatGPT to extract key takeaways
  • Turn it into a structured process you can actually follow

HERE'S HOW

For example, I took a 3-minute video from trading psychologist Brett Steenbarger and turned it into this post-trade checklist:

📺Reviewing Trading Performance

After copying the transcript into ChatGPT, use this prompt:

  • ‚ÄúHere is a transcript from a trading video. Summarise the key takeaways and create an actionable checklist that a trader can use to apply these insights in real-time. The checklist should be simple, practical, and structured for daily use.‚Äù

Then let AI do its magic‚Ä¶ tweak if needed, and you get something like this:

Post-Trade Review Checklist

  • ✅ Did I trade the right setup? (Best opportunity? Good risk-reward?)
  • ✅ Did I execute well? (Good entry? Proper size? Followed my plan?)
  • ✅ Did I manage it right? (Adjusted for market volatility? Took profits correctly?)
  • ✅ Did I stick to my rules? (Or did emotions take over?)
  • ✅ What's one thing I'll improve next session? (And how will I apply it?)

Pretty good‚Ä¶

Now, imagine doing this for:

  • üî• Mark Douglas on risk management
  • üî• Paul Tudor Jones on execution
  • üî• Jason Shapiro on strategy

(I actually ran an hour-long Jason Shapiro video through ChatGPT and asked it to summarise his strategy into a simple trading plan‚Ä¶ it did a really nice job of distilling his approach down into simple rules.)

Anyway, the sky's the limit here.

You can work backwards from what you want to improve and hunt down the right video, or watch something valuable and turn it into a structured process.

Either way, hopefully you can see how useful this can really be.

‚ÄúGreat traders are always learning.‚Äù üß†

NERVE, SELF-CONTROL, & PERSISTENCE

  • support@pepperstone.com |
  • 5:38 PM

Protect your account with two-factor authentication (2FA)

At Pepperstone, the security of your account and funds is our top priority. We are proactive about combating the growing threat of online scams, employing external technological solutions and continually reviewing our internal processes to protect you.

However, online scams are on the rise. Scammers are constantly honing their methods and finding new ways to deceive unsuspecting traders. That's why we strongly recommend that you add an extra layer of protection to your account, with two-factor authentication (2FA).

The benefits of two-factor authentication

2FA is a simple yet effective way to protect your assets from potential threats, by adding a quick extra layer to the log-in process. Enable 2FA now to:

  • Apply an extra layer of security: Even if someone steals your password, they won't be able to access your account.
  • Protect your money: Your funds remain secure, ensuring you can trade without fear of unauthorised access.
  • Prevent phishing attacks: Your personal data, and sensitive information such as bank- account information, is protected.

How to set up two-factor authentication

Setting up 2FA on your account is quick and straightforward. Just follow these steps:

  1. If you don't already have one, download an authenticator app such as Google Authenticator or Microsoft Authenticator.
  2. Log in to your Pepperstone account and tap the profile icon on the top right of the screen
  3. Go to 'view profile' which opens a new window, and select the 'two-step verification' tab
  4. Tap the 'enable two-step verification' button and follow the instructions to link it to your phone or authentication app.

Other ways to protect yourself from online scams

Traders who know how to spot scams are the least likely to fall victim to them. Here are some things to watch out for:

  • Suspicious URLs: These may be similar to Pepperstone's official site but contain small discrepancies, such as extra characters or slight misspellings.
  • Unsolicited emails: Be wary of any that claim to be from Pepperstone but contain suspicious links or ask for personal information.
  • Fraudulent online/social media ads: Fake profiles sometimes run ads promoting exclusive offers or high-return investments. Always cross-reference on our website.
  • Unofficial apps: Only download apps from official sources like the App Store and Google Play. As a precaution on Android phones, you can disable app installation from 'unknown sources' in your security settings.

You can find more information here about identifying and avoiding scams. Protecting yourself from online scams impersonating Pepperstone

The Costly Mistake of Not Sticking to Your Plan

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:08 PM

Imagine this scenario‚Ä¶

Your thesis indicates that the opening range breakout on the DAX is in play‚Ä¶and your plan is clear:

  • Enter long at 22,588
  • Stop placed at 50% of the ORB
  • Hold until the European close at 16:30 GMT

A textbook trade, right?

But then‚Ä¶ that pesky chimp brain kicks in‚Ä¶

ENTER, THE CHIMP

  • 👀 ‚ÄúLook how well the trade is doing!‚Äù
  • 👀 "It's gone straight up‚Ä¶ you should lock in profits!‚Äù
  • 👀 ‚ÄúThis month's been rough‚Ä¶ 100pts is good enough, right?‚Äù
  • 👀 ‚ÄúDon't wait for the close, this thing's gonna reverse, look!‚Äù

The logic seems sound. So, against your better judgment, you close for a quick +100pts.

Then boredom or FOMO sets in‚Ä¶

  • 👀 ‚ÄúThis thing seems overdone, I'm going to take a short scalp, stop above the high‚Äù
  1. You short for a 'quick scalp' (-41pts).
  2. You short again (-92pts), moving your stop.
  3. You add to the loser (-40pts)

Final tally? -73pts.

Had you just followed your plan and held it all day? +204pts.

Ouch.

THE REAL DAMAGE

It's not just the missed profit, it's the destructive cycle you've triggered.

  • Deviating from your plan ‚Üí Opens the door to revenge trading.
  • Closing early ‚Üí Leads to impulsive re-entries.
  • Breaking discipline ‚Üí Weakens your decision-making.

And just like that, a great trade turns into a mess.

We've all been there. But if you're still doing this, make today the day you stop.

Because the difference between a +204pt trader and a -73pt trader?

One follows the plan. The other lets emotions take over.

Trade smart. Stick to the process.

‚ÄúPlan the trade, trade the plan.‚Äù üéØ

Great traders stick to their plan.

Short Squeeze Mechanics: How to Spot & Trade Them

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:08 PM

Alright, so everyone's heard of the phrase ‚ÄúShort Squeeze‚Äù.

But what does it really mean, and what are the mechanics behind it?

First, I want to differentiate slightly between a stock short squeeze and a squeeze on, say, the indices (today's topic).

A stock short squeeze usually happens when the short float is very high, the stock is ripping to highs, and sometimes the shares loaned out are being recalled.

Check out The VW Short Squeeze for a great example:

📜The Volkswagen Short Squeeze (2008)

‚ÄúHedge-fund managers reportedly compared the Porsche disclosure to a 'nuclear bomb going off in our faces.‚Äô‚Äù

Ha! Well, that doesn't leave any doubt about the impact!!

Anyway, back to the indices‚Ä¶

SHORT SQUEEZE MECHANICS

Ok, so no one really knows how or why other participants are positioned.

For every buyer, there must be a seller‚Ä¶ throw in hedging, options, and HFTs, and you have a smorgasbord of players with different incentives and objectives.

But in simple terms, here's a good way to look at the mechanics of a short squeeze:

  • Bears see a break lower and start to pile onto the sell side, liquidating longs and initiating fresh short positions.
  • The market rebounds quickly, and it becomes clear that they've shorted into the hole.
  • So, not only do you have shorts in pain, not thinking about selling more, at best waiting to see what happens, or more likely buying to reduce their risk‚Ä¶
  • Plus, you have sidelined bulls who've been waiting for a signal to press‚Ä¶ they get long too.
  • Mid-term longs start to buy more.
  • Short-term traders start buying specifically because they see the short squeeze unfolding.

Result?

Very few sellers and an extreme supply/demand imbalance (for now).

Think about how price moves, if buyers are willing to pay higher and higher prices and sellers are happy to wait for better prices, you have a perfect storm.

Only when buyers back off the throttle and sellers start to think they need to get more aggressive with their offloads does price stall or reverse.

We don't get these often, but when we do, I think it's a potential golden opportunity.

When you look at a chart, ask yourself ‚ÄúWho is hurting the most here‚Äù

If there's been a dip that's reversed hard, it could be the shorts in a vice, and they need to cover‚Ä¶

Keep it on your radar.

Hard mode

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:01 PM

If you've ever been on one of my webinars, you've probably heard me say this (maybe too much)‚Ä¶

Stop making trading harder than it needs to be.

Especially when it comes to discipline.

Here's an analogy:

Imagine you're trying to lose weight, but you sit there staring at a fresh pizza or a big chocolate cake all day.

You only need to crack once, and you've slipped up.

You just wouldn't do that, right? You wouldn't sit there battling the urge, whispering, ‚ÄúJust one bite won't hurt‚Ä¶‚Äù

The same goes for trading.

MAKE DISCIPLINE EASIER

If you're trying to reduce impulsive trades, why sit there watching every tick, letting FOMO creep in?

Walk away. Set alerts. Step back.

If you're working on holding trades longer, why sit there staring at your P&L, broker platform open, mouse hovering over the close button?

One moment of weakness, and boom‚Ä¶you're out.

‚ÄúArgh, price is pulling back!‚Äù

Before you can calm down and rationalise why you should hold, you've already clicked exit.

So‚Ä¶ make life easier.

Sure, you could lose weight while staring at a chocolate cake all day and repeating ‚ÄúMust not eat‚Ä¶ must not eat‚Ä¶‚Äù. But let's be frank, that's the hard way.

Trading is the same.

You don't get extra points for making it difficult.

Think about what you're trying to achieve, then structure your trading environment to help you succeed.

Less friction. Less pain. More consistency.

Discipline creates success. The right broker amplifies it.

The One Hack to Cut Out Trading Noise & Stay Focused

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:04 PM

Noise isn't just indicators cluttering your chart.

It's the endless YouTube thumbnails, opinions, and clickbait titles designed to pull you in.

  • üö® ‚ÄúHow I Made $XXXK in an Hour Using This One Trick!‚Äù
  • üö® ‚ÄúThe Secret Indicator No One Talks About!‚Äù

Yawn‚Ä¶

But we've all fallen into the content rabbit hole‚Ä¶ only to realise hours later that we've learned nothing useful. Or if we did it's not actually relevant to our trading right now.

So, how do you cut through the noise and focus on what actually moves the needle?

Here's a simple tactic to try:

THE MONTHLY THEME STRATEGY

At the start of the month, decide on one key area to focus on.

It could be operational:

  • Holding trades longer
  • Trading bigger size
  • Testing a new strategy

It could be psychological:

  • Reducing FOMO
  • Eliminating revenge trading
  • Mastering discipline

Or even curiosity-based:

  • How hedge funds operate
  • The biggest market moves in history
  • Understanding options pricing

Here's how it works:

Once you pick your theme, every single piece of content you consume must align with it.

That means‚Ä¶

  • ❌ No random gold scalping tutorials
  • ❌ No getting sucked into the latest strategy videos
  • ❌ No scrolling X for market drama

Instead‚Ä¶

  • You filter out the noise
  • You absorb content that actually helps you progress
  • You train your brain to stay laser-focused on solving one problem at a time

And if you come across a video, podcast, or article that looks interesting but isn't aligned with your theme?

No problem. Bookmark it. Save it for later.

But today? You're locked in. Nothing derails your focus.

In a noisy world, it's worth a try‚Ä¶

‚ÄúGreat traders are always learning.‚Äù üß†

PLAYING CHESS

Neat TradingView Trick: Get Daily MAs on Intraday Charts

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:01 PM

A wise trader once told me: ‚ÄúMark, never trust an intraday rally when price is under the 5-day SMA‚Äù

Was this indicator BS or timeless wisdom?

Turns out, it's wisdom‚Ä¶especially during the recent sell-off.

When price is persistently below a 5-day Moving Average that's telling you something meaningful‚Ä¶. a big reprice is underway, and trying to be smart getting long is probably a trap.

Sure, you are going to miss the exact low, but this simple filter rule will save you many paper cuts along the way.

Just look at how often intraday rallies into the 5-day SMA on the Nasdaq failed recently‚Ä¶

5 DAY SMA TRICK

Simple old school rules like this can save you a lot of money.

  • ✅ Stick to shorts when price remains weak.
  • ✅ If you love buying short-term exhaustion dips intraday, fine if that's your thing, but don't overstay your welcome. A > B trades only.
  • ✅ At the very least, don't do what the crowd does: wait for strength and then pile in late (you'll just become cannon fodder for sellers).

By the way, here's a neat little TradingView trick to help:

If you want to see the daily moving average on your intraday chart, select your moving average indicator as usual, and at the bottom, instead of the default ‚Äúchart timeframe‚Äù setting, change it to 1 day.

Instantly, you've got the daily MA right there on your intraday charts.

You don't have to keep it there all day, but it's handy to quickly toggle it on and off.

Enter, the Sin Bin Strategy - your emergency plan to save your b*tt from a tilt day, week, or worse‚Ä¶

SIN BIN STRATEGY

In some sports, players who break rules get a timeout in the sin bin to cool down. Traders need something similar when discipline goes off the rails.

  • Overtrading? ‚Üí Sin bin.
  • Breaking your rules? ‚Üí Sin bin.
  • Chasing moves out of FOMO? ‚Üí Sin bin.

Step away. Reset. Let the market breathe without you forcing trades.

Most traders think they need to trade through the chaos to ‚Äúget back‚Äù what they lost. (We've all been there‚Ä¶)

That's the trap. The ones who last know when to pause.

So‚Ä¶ if you're feeling out of sync with the market, take a step back. No charts. No trades. Just give yourself time to reset.

The market will still be here tomorrow or next week.

AI RISK MANAGER

Recently I mentioned ChatGPT's new beta feature called GPT with Scheduled Tasks.

Basically, it lets you set specific tasks for ChatGPT to complete at a set time each day‚Ä¶ like a virtual risk manager nudging you before things get out of hand.

For example, you might say something like:

‚ÄúI'm a day trader, and you're my risk manager. At 10 AM each day, ask me these questions:

  1. Am I trading according to plan today, or have I gone off-track?
  2. If I've had an early loss, am I calm and clear-minded or frustrated and at risk of tilt?
  3. Am I dialled into the market, or should I step away until I'm back in sync?

Wait for my answers before continuing, and after we're done, summarise your thoughts and give me an insightful quote from a Stoic philosopher.‚Äù

You can tweak that script to fit your own trading style and issues.

Maybe you want that reminder at specific key times in the trading day. (Just after the open, Europe close, pre data, before the closing bell‚Ä¶ you get the idea.)

Sure, it's early days and a bit clunky, but think about the eventual possibilities here.

Imagine if this could be seamlessly integrated right into your trading platform, tracking your trades, spotting patterns, and calling you out before you go on tilt.

Now imagine it's hooked up to the market feed too!

üö® "Bro, better calm down‚Ä¶ you've taken two quick losses, the market is choppy. Wait for the Europe close." üòÄ

  • Traders Mastermind |

Overleveraged, oversized, and overconfident‚Ä¶ he was this close to being another trader who came and went.

He changed his entire approach to risk‚Ä¶

TRADER'S CHOICE

Rather than chasing big wins, he became obsessed with capital preservation.

He started cutting losses fast and playing great defense, which ultimately made him one of the most successful traders of all time.

His philosophy?

  • ‚ÄúThe most important rule of trading is to play great defense, not great offense.‚Äù

Most traders do the opposite‚Ä¶ they focus on making money, not keeping it.

And that's why they don't last.

Because if you don't protect your capital, you won't be around for the trades that matter.

And that doesn't just mean using a stop loss. It means:

  • Taking only high-quality trades
  • Being intentional about every decision
  • Respecting your capital like a hedge fund manager

So, let me ask you‚Ä¶

Next time you put on a trade, are you thinking defense first or just focusing on the potential gain?

Tudor Jones learned this the hard way.

You don't have to.

Something to ponder this weekend‚Ä¶

4 Steps to Detox Your YouTube Feed (And Reclaim Focus)

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:00 PM

Ah, social media, the double-edged sword‚Ä¶ The algorithm sucks you into clicking junk, but every now and then, you find real gems.

If you're like me, you try to dodge the time-wasters but still want to learn, stay sharp, and find high-quality trading content.

Snapchat? Probably not your thing. But YouTube? That one's sneaky.

It can be brilliant, some top traders drop serious value for free. But lately, it's turning into:

  • ü•± ‚ÄúHow I Made $45K Before Breakfast‚Äù
  • ü•± AI bots that ‚Äúnever lose‚Äù
  • ü•± Lambo bros selling options on stocks they can't even pronounce.

If your feed's becoming a clickbait wasteland, you're not alone.

Here's how to clean it up:

4 Steps to Fix Your YouTube Algorithm

  • Go to YouTube > History

    Delete any videos you clicked out of curiosity that don't reflect what you actually want to see more of.

  • Click the 3 dots on bad recommendations

    Choose ‚ÄúNot Interested‚Äù or ‚ÄúDon't Recommend Channel‚Äù on the recommendations page. A few of these go a long way.

  • Use Incognito mode

    If you're researching random stuff or just watching for entertainment, go incognito so it doesn't mess up your feed.

  • Train the algorithm

    Like, comment, and watch more of what is good. Subscribing (and hitting the bell) tells YouTube exactly what you want more of.

Your feed is either fueling your growth or rotting your brain‚Ä¶ might as well hack it in your favour!

PS: I know this isn't classic trading content, but protecting your focus and attention is part of the game. A clean feed = a clearer mind.

Auto tariffs jump the gun

  • Morning Bid U.S. |
  • morningbid@thomsonreuters.com |
  • 2:30 PM

High-water mark for scary US investment deficit?

One of the scariest numbers in world finance got even more frightening at the end of last year as America's skyrocketing investment deficit hit new highs. Whether it's now peaked is perhaps the most important question facing global markets today.

The main thrust of President Donald Trump's global economic policies is clearly directed toward the U.S.'s yawning trade deficit, as he seeks to stop "freeloading" foreign countries from undercutting U.S. producers by overvaluing the dollar, frustrating U.S. exports and relying on American consumers.

Valid or not, next week's sweeping U.S. import tariff hikes are aimed at correcting that.

Less talked about is the accounting flipside of the U.S. trade and current account shortfalls: the country's massive capital surplus. America, with its large, liquid capital markets, effectively imports more of the world's savings than U.S. savers send abroad to Europe, Asia or the developing world.

Put another way, the U.S. Net International Investment Position (NIIP) - or the difference in value between overseas holdings of U.S. assets and all the assets held overseas by Americans - has been ballooning for more than a decade.

According to Wednesday's update from the U.S. Bureau of Economic Analysis, that NIIP gap hit yet another record high at the end of 2024: $26.2 trillion, a whopping 88% of annual U.S. GDP. While the bulk of that increase was driven by relative price effects, it also involved almost $1.3 trillion of additional net flows to the United States.

PROJECT GATEWAY

(All insights pulled from this declassified CIA document)

📜 GATEWAY INTERMEDIATE WORKBOOK - MONROE INSTITUTE OF APPLIED SCIENCES

  1. 🎧 Binaural Beats for Brainwave Control

    The Gateway Process used specific frequencies to shift brainwaves into focused, calm, or hyper-alert states.

    ✅ As a trader:

    • Use theta (4-6 Hz) pre-market to reduce overthinking
    • Use beta (16-20 Hz) during live sessions for alertness and snap reactions

  2. üåà Color Visualisation to Shift States

    They trained subjects to associate colours with emotional states. A sort of mental shortcut.

    ✅ As a trader:

    • Blue = calm
    • Green = steady focus
    • Red = attack mode

    Trigger these visual cues before entries or post-tilt to reset your state on demand.

  3. üßò Focus 10 - Mind Awake, Body Asleep

    A core Gateway technique. You stay fully conscious while the body enters deep relaxation. Zero tension. Full presence.

    ✅ As a trader:

    Use Focus 10 before the open to stay detached, patient, and sharp when the bell rings.

  4. üß† Affirmations and Subconscious Programming

    Gateway used affirmations in altered states to reprogram beliefs and boost mental performance.

    ✅ As a trader:

    Try this:

    ‚ÄúI trade with calm confidence. I follow my plan. I accept what the market gives.‚Äù Repeat it in your morning routine‚Ä¶ or right before sleep.

  5. ‚úçÔ∏è Session Journaling for Awareness

    Gateway subjects had to log each session, tracking shifts in awareness, emotions, clarity.

    ✅ As a trader:

    Don't just track P&L.

    Log your mental state, focus level, clarity, and emotional patterns.

    Over time, you'll see what mindset leads to your best trades.

Old Map, New Terrain

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:07 PM

Sometimes it feels like every step you take is wrong‚Ä¶

  • Go long, market drops
  • Flip to short - Rallies
  • Take quick profits - trend day
  • Going to hold this one - reverses just before target

And at some point, you start questioning your damn sanity!

‚ÄúHow is it possible I'm always wrong?‚Äù

A child with a crayon and a coin would have a better return!

Here's why‚Ä¶

RHYTHM

Markets move in waves.

Even in wild conditions like these, there's still a rhythm, a structure to the way volatility expands, contracts, trends, and pulls back.

But that rhythm can shift quickly.

Sometimes intraday.

And if you're always reacting, constantly adjusting, and trading based on the last market feel, you're likely one step behind.

You're trading the prior rhythm, not the current one.

THE FIX: FILTERS

What helps?

A filter-based approach.

Instead of guessing the mood of the market, let the data decide for you.

Examples:

  • If ATR is elevated and we're breaking out on a higher timeframe ‚Üí hold for extended targets.
  • If price is range-bound and there's key econ data tomorrow ‚Üí look for A-to-B plays only.
  • Above VWAP? Long bias only. Below? Short bias - unless there's a clean exhaustion reversal.

Simple, adaptable filters like these help you sync with the current flow, not your feelings.

It's not perfect. Nothing is.

But it's a much smarter way to stay in tune with conditions and make data-driven, not emotionally-driven, decisions.

So, which filters could you implement to help stay in tune with conditions?

Your strategy, your rules.

From day trading to long-term plays, Pepperstone gives you the tools to make it happen. üî•

TIMELESS TRADING QUOTES

  1. Jesse Livermore

  2. 2. Paul Tudor Jones

    üó£ ‚ÄúI believe the very best money is made at the market turns. Everyone says you get killed trying to pick tops and bottoms, and you make all your money by playing the trend in the middle. Well for twelve years I have been missing the meat in the middle but I've made a lot of money at tops and bottoms.‚Äù

    ‚Üí Timing the turning points ‚Äî contrarian entries when others are late. But with caution! Maybe now is not the best time to explore that style‚Ä¶

  3. Stanley Druckenmiller

    ‚Äãüó£ ‚ÄúIt's not whether you're right or wrong that's important, but how much money you make when you're right and how much you lose when you're wrong - and timing is a big part of that.‚Äù

    ‚Üí Your timing amplifies or destroys the P&L profile of a trade. Pick your spots carefully, and that means sitting on your hands a lot.

  4. Marty Schwartz (Pitbull)

    ‚Äãüó£ ‚ÄúI always laugh at people who say, 'I've never met a rich technician.' I love that! It's such an arrogant, nonsensical response. I used fundamentals for nine years and got rich as a technician.‚Äù

  5. Jason Shapiro

    üó£ ‚ÄúIt's not about what the news says - it's about how the market reacts. That's where timing comes in.‚Äù

    ‚Äã‚Üí A fan favourite and for good reason. His contrarian timing is based on unexpected price reactions to expected news. Well worth thinking about in this current headline-driven environment.

  6. Mark Minervini

    üó£ ‚ÄúThe difference between a good trade and a great trade is timing.‚Äù

    ‚Üí He's big on tight entries and waiting for the right trigger condition.

  7. Linda Raschke

    üó£ ‚ÄúGood timing comes from a feel for the rhythm of the market. You can't teach it - you develop it by watching price action for thousands of hours.‚Äù

    ‚Üí Timing is intuition built through repetition. Screentime is priceless.

Capital flight fears sink dollar

  • Morning Bid U.S. |
  • morningbid@thomsonreuters.com |
  • 1:30 PM

Today's Market Minute

  • Just before President Donald Trump's social media post on Wednesday pausing tariffs, some unidentified options traders placed bets worth millions of dollars that the market would rebound, data shows. Some Democratic lawmakers are calling for investigations into whether Trump's policy reversal led to any market manipulation or insider trading.

Capital flight fears sink dollar

This all partly reflects the alarming levels of uncertainty and fears about the direction of the U.S. economy, but some economists reckon the move is also a matter of simple math. If Washington is intent on wiping out the U.S. trade deficit, it also has to accept an evaporation of the counter-balancing capital surplus, essentially the excess of overseas investments in America over U.S. investments abroad.

Weekend reading and listening suggestions

  1. Churchill and the dollar. In a column for Project Syndicate, University of California, Berkeley professor and respected currency scholar Barry Eichengreen argues the United States should heed the lessons of how sterling lost its status as the global reserve currency a century ago. "What was achieved over a long period could be demolished in the blink of an eye - or with the stroke of a president's pen."
