Monday, April 14 2025

The easiest way to build a trade idea on the fly

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:09 PM

Good morning risk taker,

Ready for another week of spicy price? üå∂Ô∏è

Good. (Not that I think we have a choice!)

So, let's kick things off with something tactical‚Ä¶

How to build intraday trade ideas on the fly.

We all know about rule-based strategies.

Stuff like the opening range breakout; very structured, clean rules, no ambiguity.

These setups are great‚Ä¶ when the market is in a certain rhythm.

  • But what about if you are a trader who is more discretionary?
  • And what about when the market changes rhythm, or just doesn't tip its hand until the bell?

How do you stay in tune with what's happening right now?

How do you walk that tightrope between reacting to price and over-planning for something that may never happen?

Here's a framework I like to use:

THE DAY TRADER'S FRAMEWORK

Filter + Trigger.

That's it.

The filter is like the safety on a weapon. No action until conditions are met.

The trigger? That's your execution point, the trade entry.

So, let's imagine we get a strong upside drive right off the open.

You don't want to chase it (smart).

But you also don't want to miss the move (also smart).

So, on the fly, you calibrate and build a few trading ideas, like this:

‚Äãüìä Example Trade Ideas:

  1. Aggressive Scalp
    • Filter: Price pulls back and trades below the 9-period SMA (1-min chart)
    • Trigger: Buy first green candle after that pullback
  2. Play the Trend
    • Filter: Price pulls back and breaches an upsloping VWAP between 3:30-6:30 pm UK
    • Trigger: Buy as price reclaims VWAP
  3. Afternoon Breakout
    • Filter: Price consolidates above VWAP and holds gains through the session
    • Trigger: Buy breakout to new highs after 6 pm UK
  4. The Trap
    • Filter: Price trends higher for 4+ hours, then reverses sharply
    • Trigger: Short on a break below the day's low

Different ideas. Same structure:

  • ✅ A clear filter and trigger
  • ✅ Proactive, not reactive
  • ✅ Built for the market you have‚Ä¶ not the market you wish for!

It's about creating clarity fast and planning your next move, under pressure, without chasing price or panicking into a trade.

Whether that's a quick scalp, or trying to get a leg in on a multi-day mover.

So, as the week unfolds‚Ä¶

Try thinking in the filters and triggers framework.

Ask yourself: ‚ÄúBased on what I see right now, what would my filter and trigger need to be for me to take the next trade?‚Äù

Let that guide your decisions, not the noise.

"Discipline in trading leads to consistency."

Easter rising? Markets seek solace

  • Morning Bid U.S. |
  • morningbid@thomsonreuters.com |
  • 1:24 PM

Today's key chart

In a world of such dramatic fundamental policy and economic disruptions, financial chart patterns and trends may seem a little beside the point. But some of these remain important for investment funds and strategists who rely on market momentum signals. One of the most basic is how the stock market is trading relative to its long-term 200-day moving average. The S&P500 fell below this on March 11 and has lost more than 500 points since then as the tariff war ensued. Another closely watched momentum signal is when the shorter-term 50-day average moves above or below the 200-day line. And it's now about to slice below it for the first time in more than a year, a move ominously dubbed a "Death Cross". The last time this happened in 2022, the S&P500 lost almost 1,000 points over the subsequent six months.

Tuesday, April 15, 2025

All Roads Seemingly Lead to a Lower USD

  • Chris Weston |
  • chris.weston@pepperstone.com |
  • 1:50 AM

An overly simplistic tactical playbook for the USD:

  • US Treasury (UST) 10 & 30yr yields trade higher, traders sell the USD vs EUR, JPY and CHF on the idea of USD repatriation flows.
  • UST yields lower, US equity higher/vol lower - traders sell the USD vs risk/high beta FX (NZD, ZAR, AUD MXN).
  • UST yields lower and equity lower/vol up, traders sell USDs vs JPY, CHF and EUR on relative haven demand - albeit, less so the CHF given the SNB may soon intervene in the FX markets.

Life is of course never this simple, and while the USD has already undergone some adjustment, in a world where probabilities matter, the odds remain stacked against the greenback.

Monday, April 21, 2025

You're Not Early. You're Just Rushing.

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:14 PM

Picture this‚Ä¶

You're stalking a long.

  • ✅ Classic double-bottom setup.
  • ✅ Rotational market.

You're looking to bid near the prior low, aiming for a mean-reversion A-to-B move back up to prior resistance.

I love these trades. Maybe you do too.

But here comes the decision:

Where exactly should you get long?

Say you're watching Crude‚Ä¶ and you spot something like this:

The Dilemma

$61 is the key support level.

Price rotated up earlier in the day, eased back, tagged $61 again, then printed a nice green candle.

Technically?

It looks good.

  • 🔹 Double bottom
  • 🔹 Whole number support
  • 🔹 Clear target
  • 🔹 Reversal bar off the level

Tempting, right?

But hold on there Mr Eager‚Ä¶

What's the trader's job?

Make the most money, with the least risk.

This setup might work.

But what's the risk?

Let's workshop it.

You'd probably place your stop just below the day's low.

Not unreasonable‚Ä¶ if it's a true ignition move, you'll be fine.

Or do you go wider to allow for a little sniff under those lows once more to ping a few stops?

And that's the issue‚Ä¶

You're either:

  • 🔹 Giving it more room. Hurting your RvR
  • 🔹 Using a tight stop. Hoping there's not a final flush before she goes.

👀 What's the Better Move?

Wait.

Wait for:

  • ✅ A retest
  • ✅ A failed break
  • ✅ A liquidity trap
  • ✅ THEN the ignition bar

You've just engineered a much better trade.

  • Higher RvR
  • Lower stop-out probability (stops already pinged)
  • Cleaner conviction

And here's what's usually missed:

If you do take the early entry and get stopped?

You'll probably want back in.

‚ÄúAh man, it was still valid. It's a stop hunt‚Ä¶. It just got me by a tick‚Ä¶‚Äù

So now you're re-entering late.

Even if that trade then works‚Ä¶ the profit on the sequence is shot because of the earlier loss‚Ä¶

üß† What's the Real Lesson?

This isn't just about being ‚Äúpatient.‚Äù That's level 1 stuff.

It's about being okay with missing trades.

You will see trades go without you.

You will miss some entries by a tick.

And that's the price you pay‚Ä¶

To only take the trades with superior structure, better risk, and cleaner logic.

Yes, it's tough.

But mastering that discomfort?

That's what separates the good from the great.

Be patient today. The best trades always stand out.

"Trading isn't just a skill, it's a mindset."

What To Do When Trading Winds You Up

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:06 PM

No matter how many thousands of hours of screen time you've racked up‚Ä¶

There will always be trades, fills, and market moves that p*ss you right off.

And here's the thing:

That won't change.

You're human.

One day, it's like water off a duck's back.

The next? Blood boiling. (Car cutting you off in traffic, anyone!?)

HOW TO MANAGE IT

Most traders fall into the trap of thinking we need to eliminate all emotion. (Hands up, I used to think this üôã‚Äç‚ôÇÔ∏è)

That's wrong.

Yes, over time, you become desensitised to certain triggers. But just like with road rage, your reaction depends on all kinds of things‚Ä¶

  • üò¥ How well you slept.
  • üòñ How stressed you are.
  • üïö Whether you've already had a tough morning.

All of it adds up.

So here's the key:

You can't control when emotion shows up.

But you can learn to recognise it‚Ä¶ and respond proactively.

Missed fill?

Got pinged out to the tick, and then price ran without you?

Whatever it is‚Ä¶

When you feel that emotion starting to build, do something now to stop it bleeding into your next decision.

  • üìâ Step away
  • üßò Do breathwork
  • üîª Dial down size

Just something to reset.

Because it's not about being emotionless.

It's about having a system for getting back to clear, focused execution despite how you feel.

However you did this week, take some time to review, reflect‚Ä¶ and then relax. And if, during that reflection, you realise too many trades were driven by emotion. Maybe now's the time to build a better defence against it.

I hate journaling

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:09 PM

‚ÄúMark, I just hate journaling. I never find the time, it's tedious, and honestly, I never review what I journal anyway.‚Äù

That's what a developing trader said to me last week.

My response?

THE PERFECT JOURNAL

‚ÄúThen don't journal.‚Äù

He looked confused.

I'm sure he expected a lecture about how ‚Äúyou MUST journal if you want any chance of making it!‚Äù

But I didn't.

In a perfect world, sure‚Ä¶ every trader would meticulously journal every detail of every trade.

But I live in the real world.

I know you've got a job, a family, commitments.

And traditional journaling takes time, time pulled from something else.

If that's you, here's the simple answer:

You have 3 minutes.

And you don't even need to be at your desk.

  • Open ChatGPT on your phone.
  • Start a new conversation.
  • Use advanced voice mode or just hit the mic icon.

(Or if you prefer, use the notes app or record a quick voice memo.)

And just talk through your trading day while it's fresh:

‚ÄúI bought the opening drive. Had my stop a bit tight. Got stopped. Market ranged for a while. I caught the break, but closed it too early‚Ä¶‚Äù

You get the idea.

No fancy tools.

No detailed stats.

Just a real-time reflection.

And here's what happens:

  • You relive the important moments of the day.
  • You see them from a calmer, post-session perspective.
  • You start to notice the same mistakes repeating.
  • You start to self-correct, naturally.

Because the real value of journaling isn't in the pretty charts.

It's in the self-awareness it creates.

If nothing else‚Ä¶ talking through your day for 3 minutes could save you months of spinning your wheels.

And my bet?

Once you start seeing the ROI from those 3 minutes, you'll naturally start going deeper and getting even more value out of it.

There's no ‚Äúright‚Äù way to trade.

Forget about what you should be doing.

This week, find your groove, and make it happen.

PS: Don't forget to join me this evening at 6pm UK for the final webinar in the Trader 2.0 series. Technical Tools Used Differently.

7 Stoic Truths for Traders

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:03 PM

Sometimes, the best trading wisdom doesn't come from modern books or flashy YT videos‚Ä¶

It comes from a Stoic philosopher born almost 2,000 years ago.

Here are 7 Epictetus quotes every trader should live (and trade) by:

EPICTETUS WISDOM

  • üèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúIt's not what happens to you, but how you react to it that matters.‚Äù
    • Losing trades. Bad fills. Fakeouts. News whipsaws.
    • All inevitable.
    • The real edge? How you respond.
  • üèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúFirst say to yourself what you would be; and then do what you have to do.‚Äù
    • Decide what trader you are.
    • Then act like it.
    • No more flip-flopping when you're bored or frustrated.
  • üèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúNo man is free who is not master of himself.‚Äù
    • Want freedom?
    • Master your emotions.
    • Freedom isn't doing whatever you feel ‚Äî it's sticking to your plan no matter what.
  • üèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúWealth consists not in having great possessions, but in having few wants.‚Äù
    • You don't need more trades.
    • You need better trades.
    • Patience > Activity.
  • üèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúIf you want to improve, be content to be thought foolish and stupid.‚Äù
    • Sometimes the best trades make you look crazy in the moment.
    • Holding firm while others panic.
    • Adding when others sneer.
    • Be willing to look wrong now‚Ä¶ to be right later.
  • ‚ÄãüèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúDon't explain your philosophy. Embody it.‚Äù
    • Forget talking about your plan.
    • Live it.
    • Day after day.
    • Results > words.
  • üèõÔ∏è ‚ÄúIt is impossible for a man to learn what he thinks he already knows.‚Äù
    • Think you've mastered trading?
    • The market will humble you.
    • Stay curious. Stay learning.

Nothing fancy today.

Just some timeless wisdom.

Maybe pick one of these quotes‚Ä¶ and actually live it next week on the screens.

Small shifts. Big results.

Catch you tomorrow, stoic.

"Discipline in trading leads to consistency.

To News or Not to News?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:09 PM

‚ÄúTo news or not to news‚Ä¶ that is the question.‚Äù - W. Shakespeare

Ok maybe he didn't say that‚Ä¶ but that's the question many traders ask themselves.

You want to stay informed.

You want to know what headlines are driving price.

But you don't want to drown in opinion pieces, Twitter spins, and mental clutter.

So what's the solution?‚Ä¶

TOXIC NEWS ANTIDOTE

  • ✅ Stick to 'real' financial news (Financial Times, Reuters, Bloomberg).
  • ✅ Follow headline sharers on X - not spin doctors. (See last week's email for my shortlist.)
  • ✅ Set strict limits - max 10 minutes of news scanning per day.

That way, you stay sharp on what matters‚Ä¶

You know what's powering the market engine - and what gear we're in.

But you don't let it cloud your thinking.

Or worse, influence your trades.

Defend that mindset at all costs.

Monday, May 5, 2025

Your pre-market prep

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:17 PM

Hope you had a refreshing weekend‚Ä¶

Let's get straight to it:

What does your pre-market routine look like?

Are you rolling out of bed, slamming a double espresso, and diving into your chair seconds before the bell?

No? Good.

Are you spending three hours analysing every chart, news item, and moon phase to prep?

Also no? Great.

The answer‚Ä¶like most things in trading, is somewhere in the middle.

Where you sit on that spectrum depends on your style and personality‚Ä¶

PRE-MARKET ROUTINE

Alright, let's build out your pre-market process.

Just a few quick checks can get you prepared mentally, operationally, and tactically for the day ahead

Non-Negotiables

  • ✅ Headline Risk - Know your scheduled econ data, central bank speeches, and potential tweet bombs.
  • ✅ Daily/Weekly Charts - Big picture. Direction. Sentiment. Bias. Don't skip it.
  • ✅ Risk Reminder - Daily loss limit, position size, max exposure. Lock it in before the heat starts.
  • ✅ Focus Cue - What are you working on right now? Holding trades longer? Taking fewer setups? Say it out loud.
  • ✅ Earnings - In season? Know what's due and what's priced in

Optional (but useful)

  • üì∞ News Scan - Quick scan of financial headlines. Real risk or fluff?
  • üéØ Bias - Have one, or don't. But decide before the bell.
  • üìç Key Levels - Areas of interest. S/R. Key levels. Gaps. You know your spots.
  • üß† Trade Ideas - Workshop some setups. Drive + pullback, flush + pop? Don't be caught shooting from the hip.

Your job as a trader?

Cover the ground that matters, efficiently. Just focus on the few elements that move the needle for you, and make them a habit.

Because that process? It tells your brain: You're in control. You're ready. You're here to take trading seriously.

Let's get after it this week, ladies and gents.

"Trading isn't just a skill, it's a mindset.

Short and sweet today, a book recommendation.

But this time, not a trading book‚Ä¶. no no.

This one's from Peter Daniel.

My pal, Level Up call host, and trader of many decades (he threatens me with violence if I reveal the exact number‚Ä¶ don't you Peter üôÇ)

THOMAS SOWELL

We were mid-curry at our favourite spot, praising capitalism, bashing socialism, as traders do‚Ä¶ When he said:

‚ÄúHave you read any of Thomas Sowell's books?‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat is he, a trader?‚Äù I asked, crunching on a poppadom.

‚ÄúNo, economist. Try his Basic Economics book‚Äù

Basic Economics? Is he taking the p*&@!?

But Peter insisted.

‚ÄúNo, honestly, it's a really good read, it makes you think about things differently. Supply and demand, pricing, it's not a trading book but it's well worth your time‚Äù

Now, Peter's not a man to make recommendations lightly, and I trust his judgement, so I ordered it on the spot.

And‚Ä¶ It's superb.

Sowell strips away jargon, tells brilliant stories, and gets you thinking differently about how prices form, why markets behave the way they do, and what actually moves the economy.

As a trader, do you need to read it?

No.

But should you?

I reckon yes.

Understanding supply and demand at a deeper level helps, even if it just sharpens how you see price.

And knowing how the bigger machine works? Can't hurt, right?

Give it a look. Basic Economics by Thomas Sowell. Cheers, Peter.

End of Month Shenanigans

Today's the final trading day of May. And May's been a beast for stock bulls.

That means two forces might be in play:

#1 Hedge funds have been scrambling to get back long (they got caught out by the snap-back rally after selling, and have been paying up to get back on board)

From: https://x.com/TheShortBear

#2 Institutional rebalancing ‚Äî big funds shifting allocations from equities (which have been super strong) into bonds (which haven't).

From: https://x.com/neilksethi

Bank of America said this:

‚ÄúWe see ~$-42bn of rebalancing flows out of equities (‚Ä¶a material ~-2.0œÉ rebalancing month)‚Äù

Translation?

Mechanical equity selling.

‚ÄúOnly part of the rebalancing is likely to be performed at month-end‚Ä¶ larger part happens at quarter-end.‚Äù

Wednesday, June 4, 2025

Marcus Aurelius knew‚Ä¶

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:03 PM

Marcus Aurelius once said:

‚ÄúHow much more harmful are the consequences of anger than the circumstances that aroused it?‚Äù

Man, I swear he was a trader‚Ä¶

Because for us, it's not the stopout, the missed fill, or the day that never got going that causes real harm.

It's what comes next:

  • üö´The hail mary revenge punt
  • ‚ùåThe oversized scalp to ‚Äúget it back‚Äù
  • ü§¨The desperate click just to feel in control

It's the reaction to the emotion, not the event, that wrecks the day.

SELF AWARE

A good trader is very self-aware.

Not robotic. Not emotionless.

Just aware of energy, focus, and especially, emotions.

You're allowed to feel frustrated.

But if you can recognise it before it infects the next trade?

  • ✅ Now you're in control.
  • ✅ Now you're trading like you know you can.

Today, pay attention to what each swing or trade does to your internal state.

Why? Because the faster you catch a shift in emotion‚Ä¶ the less power it has over your next decision.

Wed, June 11, 2025

ü§ñYou vs the VWAP Algo

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:02 PM

VWAP isn't just some random line on a chart.

It's how big players move serious size, without lighting up the tape.

üìä According to BestEx Research, 72% of institutional traders use VWAP algos for low-urgency orders. BestEx Research Debuts 'New Category of Execution Algo'

Why?

Because the job of a VWAP algo is simple:

üëâ Fill the order at or better than VWAP.

Let's break this down‚Ä¶see if we can find some edge here.

VWAP EDGE

Picture this‚Ä¶

You're an algo with 10,000 contracts of Nasdaq futures to sell.

You can't just slam the market, right? That would cause massive slippage.

But NQ trades ~400k contracts a day, so if you slice it up, feed it slowly, and follow the volume, you might just get it done quietly‚Ä¶ and at a good average price.

So you load the sell order into a VWAP algo.

Now‚Ä¶ let's zoom in.

‚Äãüö® The Turning Point

The algo's been working the order all morning.

Filled ~35% of the size.

VWAP is sitting nicely below the current market.

Life is good.

But there's a problem:

The clock's ticking, and price is drifting too far above VWAP.

From the algo's point of view:

‚ÄúI'm ahead of schedule and getting better-than-VWAP fills. Great. But I still have 65% left. Anything can happen. Let's get moving before this slips away‚Ä¶‚Äù

So it starts selling more aggressively:

Hitting bids. Working harder. Getting filled faster. Other algos with similar orders start doing the same.

And then?

  • Selling pressure increases
  • The market starts to roll
  • Price magnetises back to VWAP

Not because the buyers vanished‚Ä¶

But because the bots are doing their job.

‚Äãüìâ When Price Meets VWAP Again‚Ä¶

  • The aggressive selling slows.
  • The algo calms down.

And ‚Ä¶

üí° Buy-side VWAP algos might now see price as attractive. So they quietly start working their orders too‚Ä¶ Adding subtle buying pressure right where the sell-side was just active.

‚Äãüîç So what's the takeaway for us?

Understanding how and why VWAP algos behave gives you a real edge.

  • It explains those repeatable mid-day rolls.
  • It offers clues on hidden intent.
  • It helps you build plays around their behaviour.

üìΩ My ‚Äú6 o'clock shock‚Äù strategy is built on this exact idea, riding the curl in price as the VWAP algos kick into more aggressive gear.

üëâüèªWatch the video [here]. VWAP Trading Strategies - Trend and mean reversion setups

Even if that play is not your thing, I think understanding the motivation and behaviour of 'big money' can really help you identify edge‚Ä¶

Enjoy the rabbit hole üòÅ

1980s TRADER

  • #1 Cut Your Losses Fast

    In one scene, Paul goes massively long index futures. (About 23mins in) Full conviction. One of his biggest positions ever.

    But when the market turns, he dumps the entire trade for a 5% hit ‚Äî $6 million loss.ü§ï

    Why?

    Because price matters more than your opinion. Always.

  • #2 Emotion Isn't Weakness

    He's visibly shaken after the loss.

    Agitated. Frustrated.

    And then he says:

    ‚ÄúIt's painful to give profits back‚Ä¶
    It's a mental blow, an intellectual blow.
    But it's part of the business.‚Äù

    He feels it, like we all do, but stays composed.

  • #3 Holding Winners is Hard

    A couple of months later, he's heavy long again.

    Millions in unrealised profit.

    He says:

    ‚ÄúI want to sell so bad I can't stand it‚Ä¶
    But I need to sit back.‚Äù
    ‚ÄúI'm so long I'm scared to death.‚Äù

Sound familiar? üòÅ

He holds. Market rips to new all-time highs.

That's the game.

It's not about being perfect.

Even billionaire traders second-guess themselves.

But they follow the core rules:

  • üìâ Cut the losers
  • üìà Ride the winners
  • üß† Stay calm

Friday, June 13, 2025

The Replay Ritual That Sharpens Your Edge

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:02 PM

So, I have to hold my hands up here‚Ä¶ I was slow to adopt market replay.

Love tech, love AI‚Ä¶ but when it came to trade reviews, I stuck with printed charts and a pencil.

Old habits‚Ä¶ (Still bitter about the time my data provider changed the Level 2 colours in 2010) üò¨

But now?

I'm converted.

Market replay is a game changer.

It shows you things no journal or screenshot ever could:

  • What really happened before and after your entry
  • How price moved‚Ä¶ not how you remember it üòÅ
  • Where the execution could've been better
  • And the one tweak that changes everything next time

If you want to explore market replay, here's the framework I've found to be pretty good‚Ä¶

REPLAY FRAMEWORK

This weekend, replay 2 trades:

Your best and your worst.

(And ‚Äúworst‚Äù doesn't have to mean losing, it could be a rule break or missed exit.)

Fire up replay. I use TradingView, and FYI, Pepperstone's running a free access deal for clients, existing and new, right now.

Then run through this checklist:

  • ✅ What was I seeing at the time?

    Narrate your thoughts before entry. What was the thesis, and what made you pull the trigger?

  • ✅ What did price do just before/after?

    Replay it slowly, did you miss any tells?

  • ✅ Was the entry optimal?

    Could you have waited? Entered better? Avoided it?

  • ✅ What did I miss?

    Context clues, time of day, VWAP, volume, HTF bias?

  • ✅ How did I manage the trade?

    Did you hold, size up/down, move stops?

  • ✅ Where was the best exit?

    Replay what happened after, where should/could you have reasonably closed?

  • ✅ Was there a better variation of this idea?

    Breakout vs pullback after breakout? Pinbar trap vs momentum ignition?

  • ✅ Key takeaway?

    One tweak to apply next time this play appears.

Try it this weekend, just 20 minutes.

Quick to do, massive ROI.

This is the kind of work most traders skip‚Ä¶

Which is exactly why it gives you the edge.

If you want to dial your replay ritual up even more, my Missing Edge webinar replay is now live.

Stay safe online - protect your account

  • Pepperstone Support |
  • support@pepperstone.com |
  • 6:39 PM

Stay alert

Identify scammers and protect your account

Online scammers use fake search results, phishing emails, and deceptive websites to impersonate trusted companies like Pepperstone and steal personal data. Traders who know how to spot the signs are less likely to fall victim.

What to watch out for

Suspicious URLs: Fake websites with URLs similar to Pepperstone's official site that often include extra characters or subtle misspellings.They may appear via

  • Online search engines using similar branding, logos, and design.
  • Phishing emails asking for login, payment or personal details.
  • Social media ads from fake profiles promoting exclusive offers. Always cross-reference on our website

Enable 2FA to protect your account

For an extra layer of security, follow the simple steps below to enable 'Two Factor Authentication (2FA)'

  1. If you don't already have one, download an authenticator app such as Google Authenticator or Microsoft Authenticator.
  2. Log in to your Pepperstone account and tap the profile icon on the top right of the screen.
  3. Go to 'view profile' which opens a new window, and select the 'two-step verification' tab.
  4. Tap the 'enable two-step verification' button and follow the instructions to link it to your phone or authentication app.

You can find more information about identifying and avoiding scams here. Protecting yourself from online scams impersonating Pepperstone

Your security is our top priority

Please remain vigilant and report any suspicious activity to our support team at support@pepperstone.com.

ChatGPT to name your playbook??

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:02 PM

Linda Raschke was one of the first traders to give her setups names you couldn't forget.

ü©≥ Short Skirt Trade - Quick in and out before anyone notices.

üê∂ Burning Dog - No one wants to touch it.

And sure, the names are fun‚Ä¶

But they're also powerful mental anchors.

Because when you give your setups a sharp, memorable name, you give your subconscious a cue:

‚ÄúThis is that trade, with this logic, these rules, and this objective.‚Äù

No more turning a scalp into a swing.

No more letting a strict setup become a vague 'maybe'.

But naming them is the hard part.

So, enter our good old friend ChatGPT‚Ä¶ with this prompt:

NAME YOUR SETUPS

Here's the prompt:

I want you to help me come up with a sharp, memorable name for a specific trading setup I use.

The goal: The name should act as a mental shortcut that instantly reminds me of the setup's core logic.

It should reflect either:

  • - The pattern itself
  • - The intention behind the trade
  • - The constraints (time, signal, target, narrative)
  • - Or the emotional discipline required to execute it

Start by asking me:

  1. What is the setup?
  2. When do you take it?
  3. What's the entry trigger?
  4. What's the typical target?
  5. What makes this trade work ‚Äî or fail?
  6. Do you want the name to sound tactical, analytical, cheeky, clean, poetic, or prop-style?

Then give me 5-10 name options that reflect those answers ‚Äî mixing styles if useful ‚Äî and include a short line explaining why each name fits.

Make sure each name reinforces proper execution.

You might need to tweak and reply a few times to get what you want, but it's worth doing.

I used this to name one of my opening drive scalp plays.

10AM Guillotine.

‚Äãüí• Brutal. Precise. Done by 10AM.

That name reminds me exactly what this trade is supposed to be.

And that alone keeps me from overtrading it.

Try it with one of your setups, see what it comes up with!

This ChatGPT trick saved me 10 hours of research

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 1:04 PM

ChatGPT just changed the game for market research.

And by ‚Äúresearch,‚Äù I don't mean hours of reading papers or squinting at news sites‚Ä¶

I mean a one-line prompt that gives you a clear edge when the market throws something unexpected at you.

Let me show you what I'm talking about‚Ä¶

g

WHEN IRAN HIT THE HEADLINE

When the U.S. struck Iran recently, traders scrambled to figure out the impact.

  • Would the oil spike hold?
  • Would equities crash?
  • What about gold and the dollar?

Most traders were guessing.

Unless you're an expert in Middle East geopolitics‚Ä¶ it's all noise.

But here's what I typed into ChatGPT:

"How did oil, gold, equities, and USD respond during past Iran-related conflicts?‚Äù

And in seconds:

  • Strait of Hormuz attacks (2019): Oil +10%, faded quickly
  • Soleimani strike (2020): Crude spiked, gold ran, ES dipped, all reversed in days
  • Breakdown of timelines, price reactions, duration of moves

Then I asked:

‚ÄúWhat did Iran do militarily after the U.S. killed Qasem Soleimani in 2020? Include missile strikes, cyberattacks, and how oil & equities responded.‚Äù

Now I'm a geopolitical analyst with data-backed context (minus the 10 hours of doomscrolling.) üòÅ

What did I learn?

  • Iran saved face without triggering a war
  • Closing the Strait was always unlikely
  • Oil spiked, equities wobbled‚Ä¶ then both cooled off fast

From this, I could:

  • Understand likely market reactions to current events
  • Avoid impulsive trades on opinions
  • Layer that into my trade ideas

And this is just one use case‚Ä¶

I think we forget‚Ä¶ You can ask anything:

  • ‚ÄúWhich sectors rally after CPI beats vs. misses?‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúHow often does Tesla reverse after a big earnings-day gap?‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúWhich stocks have the biggest intraday moves after missing earnings?‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúWhat's the average Nasdaq return after a -2% day?‚Äù

Basically:

  • You now have a research team on tap‚Ä¶ for free.
  • You just need to ask the right questions.
  • Thanks, Mr Altman‚Ä¶

PS: Got any cool ChatGPT use cases of your own?

Monday, June 30, 2025

Picking a fight you can't win

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:01

Once, I watched a guy try to square up to a bouncer.

6'5‚Äù, arms like tree trunks, just waiting for an excuse to flatten someone.

The other guy?

Maybe 5'7‚Äù, scrawny dude‚Ä¶ but full of attitude and delusion.

Thought he could win. Thought this was his moment.

It ended exactly how you'd expect. ü§ï

Be the Lion, Not the Idiot

Think about a lion for a moment, king of the jungle.

Fierce. Deadly. Apex predator.

But he doesn't chase everything.

He doesn't charge a full-grown elephant.

He doesn't sprint into a herd of buffalo.

He waits.

He watches.

He picks the moment with the highest probability of success:

  • ü¶å A weak deer straying from the herd
  • ü•§ A youngster drinking alone
  • üêæ A tired, limping target

The lion is lethal because he's selective.

He knows his edge. He protects his resources.

He only strikes when the odds are stacked in his favour.

If he chased every opportunity?

He'd burn out. Starve. Die.

Now‚Ä¶ think about your trading.

Every setup is not your setup.

Every market is not your opportunity.

If you're forcing trades in dead zones, fighting chop, chasing every candle‚Ä¶ You're the guy swinging at the bouncer.

üß† Today, think like a lion:

  • Wait for your advantage
  • Preserve your capital
  • Press hard only when the odds are stacked in your favour

Let others fight over scraps.

You wait for the kill shot.

"Trading isn't just a skill, it's a mindset."

Wednesday, July 2, 2025

A 'Golden Cross' Triggered on the S&P500:

Why Traders Should Look Elsewhere

  • Chris Weston |
  • chris.weston@pepperstone.com |
  • 5:20

The financial media has been quick to highlight the recent ‚Äúgolden cross‚Äù on the S&P 500 - where the 50-day moving average (MA) has crossed above the slower 200-day MA. While this crossover may be loosely viewed as a bullish entry signal, does it really offer positive expectancy for short-term CFD traders?

In my view, the answer is no.

By its nature, the golden cross signals that underlying index momentum is strong - something already evident in the price action. The S&P 500 has rallied an impressive 28% from the April lows, trading at new all-time highs. That alone tells us what we need to know: momentum is intact.

For those deploying momentum or trend-following strategies, a shorter-term MA crossover system is arguably a better tool - either as a component in trade entry or more effectively, as a systematic exit trigger.

One example: I use the 3- & 8-day EMA crossover as a clean exit strategy on higher timeframes. It helps reduce emotional decision-making, allowing me to stay in trending trades longer without the temptation to ‚Äúbuy the dip‚Äù and reload at wider spreads. Staying in the trend is the goal - simple systems like this help achieve it.

These basic signals may seem overly simplistic to some. Yet over time, many traders find themselves stripping back complex exit models to simpler rules: a moving average crossover, a trailing ATR stop, or a rolling 20-, 40-, or 65-day low. Clean. Objective. Repeatable.

Does the Golden Cross Offer Any Edge?

Let's test the golden cross historically on the S&P 500:

  • Since January 2000, there have been 11 prior golden cross events.
  • If a trader had bought the S&P 500 on the day of the signal and held for 50 trading days, they would've been in the money 9 out of 11 times (82% win rate), with an average gain of 5%.
  • The two losing trades averaged a loss of -0.9%.

So yes, historically the golden cross aligns with further gains on average, but the sample size is statistically insignificant, and the signal is lagging by design.

Take the last golden cross on 2 February 2023 - the S&P 500 reversed sharply on the same day and fell 9.2% over the next 26 days.

Why It Doesn't Work for Short-Term CFD Traders

For short-term traders, especially in CFDs, the golden cross is too slow and lacks actionable timing precision. Markets today are far more dynamic , and the structure has changed dramatically:

  • High-frequency trading (HFT) now accounts for 70-80% of S&P 500 daily volume.
  • 0DTE options dominate, making up over 50% of daily notional options turnover.
  • Leverage ETF & other passive flows, increasingly drive intraday volatility.

Add to that the constant real-time influence of Trump's social media posts, pending macro catalysts (like the OBBB Act, U.S. Q2 earnings season starting July 15), and data-driven market reactions, and it's clear: price is the first derivative and leads, not MAs.

The S&P 500 has now rallied 832% since the 2009 lows - not because of golden crosses, but because buying weakness in a structurally rising market has worked. That's a far more powerful message for investors and traders alike.

Conclusion

Yes, historically golden crosses coincide with further gains. But for short-term traders, especially those using CFDs, this signal offers no real edge. Instead, focus on faster momentum signals, reactive price-based strategies, or MA systems with a tighter lookback period.

The weird trick Tony Robbins stole from Pavlov üß†

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

Ever heard of anchoring? (Not the kind you do with your yacht off some private island‚Ä¶üòÅ)

It's the idea that you can take a specific physical gesture, like clenching your fist, tapping your chest, or gripping the steering wheel‚Ä¶ and link it to a mental state.

It's just Pavlov's dog, but make it‚Ä¶ performance psychology.

(You remember that one‚Ä¶ the bell rings, dog salivates.)

Same concept.

Except you're the dog. And the bell? That's whatever trigger you choose.

Tony Robbins bangs on about this a lot.

He'll get someone into a peak emotional state first. Think, power, focus, confidence and then get them to anchor it to a motion.

Touch your heart. Click your fingers. Clench your fist.

Do it enough times, and the body remembers.

The trigger fires > state kicks in.

Now let's bring that to trading‚Ä¶

You want more discipline? Anchor it.

Before you hit buy/sell‚Ä¶ Before you even sit down at the desk‚Ä¶

  • üí• Tap your chest
  • üí• Take a sharp breath
  • üí• Repeat a phrase (‚Äúcalm, sharp, focused‚Äù)

But here's the trick:

You have to build the association first.

Anchor the state when you're feeling it:

  • ✅After a great trade.
  • ✅After a solid day
  • ✅After reviewing a journal entry where you stuck to the plan.

That's when you lock it in. You're not just feeling good, you're teaching your system what that feels like.

So, next time you're in that zone, calm, clear, dialled in. Pick a cue. Tap. Breathe. Press your fingers. Something simple and repeatable.

Then, before each trade: Trigger it.

Let it bring you back into that mental gear.

Do this consistently, and it becomes automatic.

The body leads. The mind follows.

Soon enough, like Pavlov's dog at the sound of a bell‚Ä¶ You'll find yourself stepping into discipline with a single cue.

(Not drooling‚Ä¶ üòÅ)

Give it a go. You might be surprised how well it works.

"Your edge in trading begins with discipline."

Thursday, July 3, 2025

Just enough success to ruin you‚Ä¶

  • Traders Mastermind
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

Peter Brandt recently said this‚Ä¶

And he's right‚Ä¶

Whether you're a 'young' or erm 'not so young' trader, the reason you got into this business was because you believed you could make it happen.

Right?

Else, why would you bother?

So, by that measure, we can assume most traders are driven, ambitious, and believe they have the character to win.

Enter: Unrealistic expectations, stage left.

EXPECTATIONS

Unlike, say, brain surgery or flying a 747‚Ä¶ there's basically zero chance you could do either of those without serious training. Years of it. Supervised. Structured.

But trading?

There's this slim chance you could do very well, very quickly.

And that's where the real danger begins.

Because, unlike flying a plane, where your incompetence is immediately obvious‚Ä¶üòÅ

Trading gives you just enough success to believe you're different.

A few green days. A lucky runner. One home-run setup that worked out perfectly.

You start thinking, ‚ÄúI've got this. I'm close.‚Äù

But now you're no longer just learning the craft. Now you're carrying expectations.

And they're a heavy burden to bear:

  • You expect to grow your account every month.
  • You expect to bounce back quickly from drawdowns.
  • You expect to be immune to tilt, fear, hesitation.
  • You expect your potential to show up just because you want it more than most.

Peter's right‚Ä¶ nobody talks about this part.

Not the trades. The internal pressure.

The voice that says:

  • ‚ÄúYou've been doing this too long to still be struggling.‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúYou're better than this.‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúYou should be making X by now.‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúPeople are watching.‚Äù

That voice gets louder after a few wins. It doesn't go away with screen time. It grows with progress, and crushes you when the results don't match your expectations.

The hardest part of trading isn't strategy.

It's dealing with the gap between:

  • üß† What you think should be happening‚Ä¶
  • Vs.
  • üìâ What's actually happening.

Bridging that gap is the real work.

It's not glamorous. It's not sexy. And nobody's posting about it.

But it's the game.

Keep showing up. Drop the self-imposed pressure.

Mastery takes longer than your ego wants it to.

Have a great (half) trading day.

‚ÄúA good trader plays the long game.‚Äù üîÑ

Drone Swarm, Not Cannons

  • Traders Mastermind
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:03

Yesterday I was reading about a new weapon the UK's developed called the RapidDestroyer.

(Pleased to see they spent the budget on the weapon‚Ä¶ not the naming committee üòÜ)

If you're curious, it's basically a massive portable microwave that fries drones mid-flight.

Cos, we've all seen those drone swarms, right?

Thousands of them flying in sync, lighting up the Beijing sky. Now imagine them armed with explosives instead of LEDs‚Ä¶ üò¨

Anyway, I've veered off into armchair weapons expert territory. Let's get back to trading.

What the hell does this have to do with trading, Mark?

Well, it got me thinking‚Ä¶

DRONE SWARM MODE

You've got to fight the battle you're given, not the one you wish you were in.

That's what good traders do.

We might want clean trend days‚Ä¶

We might hope for that nice 10 am reversal off VWAP‚Ä¶

We might wish crude oil to respect that tight channel we drew last night‚Ä¶

But the market doesn't care what we want.

Sometimes it's choppy.

Sometimes it's slow.

Sometimes it's irrational, overlapping, stop-hunting chaos.

And the faster we accept that, the faster we stop trying to force our strategy onto a battlefield that's already changed.

The best traders?

They don't bring a knife to a gunfight. Or a breakout play to a mean-reverting mess.

They stay alert to changing conditions, intraday or intra-quarter.

They adapt.

They deploy the right weapon at the right time‚Ä¶ or sit tight until the battlefield shifts.

So here's a challenge this week:

  • üëä What setup are you forcing right now just because it worked last month?
  • üëä What market are you trading just because you're comfortable with it (even if it's sloppy)?
  • üëä And if your current edge isn't working, are you reviewing the conditions, not just the entries?

Worth a thought before the next drone swarm hits‚Ä¶

Because sometimes it's just one small shift‚Ä¶ A minor calibration‚Ä¶ That gets you back on track.

📆 25th April 2016 ‚Äî ‚ÄúThe Most Hated Rally I've Ever Seen‚Äù

📆 3rd June 2020 ‚Äî ‚ÄúThe Most Hated Rally In History Just Won't Stop‚Äù (Bloomberg)

The market didn't give a sh*t who hated it. It just kept going.

  • It defies logic or fundamentals
  • Analysts can't reconcile it with PE ratios or recession fears
  • It feels like a bubble
  • Everyone's expecting a collapse

When Wall Street hates a rally, it usually means they're lagging the benchmark‚Ä¶ and hating every damn minute of it!

And that brings us to today:

  • üò°Another hated rally.
  • üò°Another group of reluctant buyers.
  • üò°Another round of ‚ÄúThis can't keep going‚Ä¶‚Äù as it keeps chugging.

Maybe.
Probably not.

Does it matter?

Nope.

If the market keeps climbing, as traders we keep buying dips, playing support, riding the wave.

If it rolls over, great‚Ä¶ we all love a clean short!

Either way, the lesson's the same:

  • üí° Sentiment drives moves.
  • And ‚Äúhated‚Äù doesn't mean ‚Äúover.‚Äù

Because let's be honest‚Ä¶
They have to buy it.

Not because they love it, but because God forbid they miss the move while everyone else rides it higher.

Far better to be wrong with the herd than be the only genius who sat out and got fired for underperformance.

‚ÄúYeah, boss, I didn't buy the rally because I hated it.‚Äù

Clear your mind. Trade what's in front of you.

  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

On Tuesday, I had a call with a trader who's deep into Phase 2 of his strategy.

The challenge?

His single-instrument setup was working beautifully. Several strong months, solid size, consistent results.

But, there were prolonged periods of no trades, and he wanted to kick things up a gear, without breaking what was already working.

So, we jumped on a call and workshopped it through‚Ä¶

PHASE 2

After the standard British whinge about the heat, üòÅ we got down to brass tacks and laid out a few possible paths:

  1. Tweak the strategy to trigger more often
  2. Add one or two new markets during the same execution window
  3. Trade another market in a different time window
  4. Increase size
  • üö´ More size? Off the table (for now). He was already pushing enough; ¬£8k green days weren't uncommon, and the margin requirements meant he would have to deposit a big chunk of extra cash into his account.
  • üö´ Adjusting the strategy for more frequency? Hmm, I didn't like it. Could dilute the already working edge.
  • üö´ Trading in a different time window? Naa. He liked his current workflow and didn't want to mess with it. As tempting as it is to add more work, remember that focus and energy aren't infinite.
  • ‚Äã‚úÖ So we settled on adding new markets in the same window.

Then he said something interesting:

‚ÄúI only want to take shorts. I prefer shorting. I'm happy just waiting for the right setup.‚Äù

And I thought: perfect.

That's what Steenbarger always says‚Ä¶

‚ÄúElite performers don't just fix weaknesses‚Ä¶ they double down on strengths.‚Äù

This trader was already good and had killer potential‚Ä¶
If he wanted to laser focus on what he was good at, then great.

So, we added two uncorrelated markets for short-only entries, and he left with a plan to run some low-R unit tests and build from there.

Ok, why am I telling you this?

  1. When you hit a challenge, take the time to map the options. The obvious path isn't always the best one.
  2. Play to your strengths. If you're better at shorts, focus there. If you trade best in short bursts, design around that.
  3. Then craft a plan, back it, and move.

The ‚ÄúAlways In A Trade‚Äù Game üß†

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:03

Trading is serious business.

But sometimes‚Ä¶ the best way to improve is to make parts of it fun, right?

ALWAYS IN

Picture this:

You've hit your daily loss limit or your target.
Maybe the market's choppy.
You know you should be done for the day.

But‚Ä¶ you still want to watch tape.
You still want to trade.
You still want to learn...

Enter: The Always In Game.

(Disclaimer: walking away is the right call ‚Äî but if this helps you avoid revenge trading on your live account, it might be worth it.)

Here's how it works:

  • Load up a demo account or trade with tiny size
  • You must always be in the market: long or short
  • You can't close a position‚Ä¶ only reverse
  • Run it for one hour
  • Try to make as much as possible

Why bother?

  • It keeps you off your live account when you know you shouldn't be trading
  • It trains your tape reading in a unique way‚Ä¶ You can't just ‚Äúexit.‚Äù You must commit or reverse. Tough.
  • It gives your ‚Äúchimp brain‚Äù something to chew on so you still feel productive (a common challenge for part-time traders‚Ä¶I'm at the screen, so I need to do something)

Because sometimes, taking things less seriously‚Ä¶ leads to better results.

Give it a try. Might surprise you. üòé

Old School Trading Sayings That Refuse to Die

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

Markets change.
Tech evolves.
‚Äã(Imagine telling Jesse Livermore about ChatGPT‚Ä¶ ‚Äúyeah, so there's this device in your pocket that knows everything right, and‚Ä¶‚Äù)

But some old-school trading sayings?
Well, they stick around for a reason.

Here are 5 classic adages that still hold weight today‚Ä¶

TRADING ADAGES

üìà ‚ÄúStrong stocks close strong.‚Äù

Don't overthink it. If a market holds highs all day and closes near the high, there's usually follow-through coming. The strength is telling you something‚Ä¶ Hold.

üß® ‚ÄúDon't short a dull market.‚Äù

Sideways, quiet sessions are a trap for short sellers. Without urgency, price often just grinds higher and wrecks your patience. Shorts thrive in momo.

üï∞ ‚ÄúAmateurs open the market, pros close it.‚Äù

Sure, it's mostly algos now, but the close still matters.
It's where the auction ends, the final agreed price‚Ä¶ and the one that makes the headlines.

üîÑ ‚ÄúCut your losers fast, let your winners run.‚Äù

Clich√©? Yes.
Ignored by 90% of traders? Also yes.
But it's still one of the most important rules in the game.

ü´£ ‚ÄúThe market can stay irrational longer than you can stay solvent.‚Äù

Thinking you're smarter than price is the fastest path to pain. Ride the wave, don't fight the tide.

Old traders knew the score‚Ä¶
‚ÄúThe markets may change, but human nature never does.‚Äù

Very true, gentlemen. Very true.

Who are you?

  • Traders Mastermind |

  • What type of trader are you?
  • What do you believe?
  • What are you good at or getting good at?
  • What game do you play?

Because trading's a game of infinite variables, right?

  • üëâüèª Market
  • üëâüèª Timeframe
  • üëâüèª Strategy
  • üëâüèª Risk approach
  • üëâüèª Add or don't add
  • üëâüèª Cut quickly or let it breathe
  • üëâüèª Scalp or hold

DEFINE YOUR GAME

What are you focusing on?
What are you trying to master?

But if you're chasing every style, every setup, every market‚Ä¶

You become a jack of all trades, and the market doesn't pay generalists.
It pays specialists. (Doesn't matter what you specialise in, just that you do.)

So today, take 60 seconds to pause and ask:

  • ✅ What's my game?
  • ✅ What am I getting exceptional at?
  • ✅ What can I ignore?

Thursday, August 7, 2025

üë®üèº‚Äçüî¨Trading Science Experiments

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

I often think of trading like a science experiment.

And I'm the, ahem, 'mad' scientist‚Ä¶
Tinkering, testing, refining, always looking for edge.

To keep it simple, I bucket my experiments into four categories‚Ä¶

TRADING SCIENCE EXPERIMENTS

  • üß™ Lose Less ‚Äî Reduce losses, magnitude and frequency.
  • üß™ Win More ‚Äî Improve win rate on trades.
  • üß™ Make More on Winners ‚Äî Extract more from the winning trades.
  • üß™ Find New Setups ‚Äî Explore strategies worth adding to the playbook.

And so when I use buckets like this, I know exactly what the outcome should be.

So, let's say I'm in deep operational mode and looking at how the TICK index can help fine-tune a pullback entry.
(I've done some good training on the TICK index here ‚áí Short Term Trading Strategies Using The TICK Index - A Day Trader's Quick Guide

That's a Win More experiment. I'm not trying to bank more on each trade, just hit a higher win rate by improving timing.

Or maybe I'm reviewing stop losses in my journal‚Ä¶

  • Do I need the full stop here?
  • Should I be scaling out sooner on certain setups?
  • Are some plays producing too many full stops, and are they worth it?

That's squarely in the Lose Less bucket

And that's the point:

When you define the type of experiment, you stop obsessing over the P&L (which is often a lagging indicator)

And start measuring success by the outcome you intended.

Try it.

Pick a bucket.
Run the test.
Review the result.

You're not just a trader‚Ä¶
You're the CEO of your trading business.
Allocating time, focus, and capital to the experiments that drive the highest return.

Wednesday, August 13, 2025

Are stop losses ruining your edge?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:03

Are stops ruining your edge?

Now that's an emotive question right‚Ä¶!?

Before you sharpen the pitchforks üòÄ, yes, of course I'm a fan of cutting losers.
Risk management is non-negotiable.

But trading is about thinking, testing, experimenting‚Ä¶ so let's poke the bear:
maybe hard stops aren't all they're cracked up to be.

NO STOPS?

Don Miller - one of the first trading bloggers who documented his $1.6m day trading run ‚Äî once said: (and I'm paraphrasing here)

‚ÄúI don‚Äôt use stops. I manage risk with size.‚Äù

Meaning he only used a hard stop as a last resort, sizing positions so he could manage exits manually.

Larry Connors found that his mean reversion trades performed best with no stops at all.

And random walk theory? It says the probability of your stop getting hit is twice the probability of price actually closing beyond it.

Translation: once you're stopped, the odds flip to 50/50 of it coming right back.
(Not sure I fully buy that‚Ä¶ but you get the idea)

At some point, you need to exit a losing trade, that's a given, but exiting via a hard stop all the time, well, that might not be the best bet.

So, what else can you do?

  • Manual Exit: Watch the price action and close if the trade's no longer valid. (Disciplined? Great. Rule-breaker? Dangerous.)
  • Time-Based Stop: Review at a fixed time ‚Äî hold, close, or adjust. Favoured by swing traders.
  • Hybrid: Keep an ‚Äúemergency‚Äù hard stop but actively manage, trim, or exit before it's hit.

I might have just opened a can of worms here‚Ä¶ but it's worth asking:

Is slapping a hard market order stop on every trade actually helping your edge, or quietly killing it?

Someone's got to ask the unpopular questions!

Monday, August 18, 2025

Day vs Swing Trading: Should You Switch? ü§î

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:01

‚ÄúHow do you transition from day trading to swing trading without losing momentum?‚Äù

I saw this question the other day and thought I'd share my take‚Ä¶ because it's not the first time I've heard it.

DAY TRADING vs SWING TRADING

The first thing to ask yourself is simple: why do you want to make the shift?

  • üëâ Is it because your schedule has changed and you can't be glued to the screens all day?
  • üëâ Is it because the constant screentime focus of intraday trading is draining you?
  • üëâ Or is it because your results aren't where you want them to be, and you're hoping swing trading will ‚Äúfix‚Äù that?

That last one matters.

Because if discipline and execution are the issue, changing the timeframe won't solve the root cause. (It just moves the same habits into a different tf.)

Now, the trade-offs:

Pros of swing trading

  • Calmer, less rushed decision-making. You've got time to plan rather than react.
  • Potentially better risk-to-reward ratios. You're no longer capped by the day's range.
  • More space to let themes and trends play out.

Cons of swing trading

  • ‚úò Overnight risk. Gaps can and will catch you out. (depending on the market)
  • ‚úò Tape-reading edge doesn't translate well.
  • ‚úò Far fewer trade reps. Instead of 5-10 trades a day, maybe you're getting a handful per month. That slows the learning curve.

So what's the play?

If you're considering the switch, why not do both for a while?

Keep a portion of your focus on intraday trades, but layer in swing positions on the side.

That way, you'll see firsthand if the swing approach suits your temperament without throwing away the reps and data you're getting from day trading.

Because the real edge isn't in ‚Äúday vs swing.‚Äù
It's in knowing which style fits your personality, goals, and life outside the market.

And maybe the answer isn't ‚Äúswitch.‚Äù
Maybe it's ‚Äúdo both‚Äù... and lean into whichever gives you the edge right now.

Market regime, goals, resources, skill set‚Ä¶ they all shift. Your job as a trader is to carve out edge.

And when you do have momentum? Push. Push hard. Momentum is the lifeblood of great trading. Don't pivot when things are working üòé

Thursday, August 21, 2025

Conviction vs. Noise (Which One Are You Trading?)

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

If you're not sure about a trade‚Ä¶ just leave it.

We've all been there. Market's moving, volatility's high, but the setup isn't quite there.

So we squint, tilt our heads, convince ourselves it's a trade, and hit buy/sell.

Even if it wins, here's the problem:

CONVICTION

Without conviction, the trade is doomed.

Think about it:

With Conviction

  • You're unfazed if it takes some heat. Stop is in, no worries.
  • If it pauses on the way to target? Normal ebb and flow. You hold.

No Conviction

  • It ticks against you: ‚ÄúKnew I shouldn't have taken it‚Äù ‚Üí cut early.
  • It stalls in profit: ‚ÄúDon't want it to come back‚Äù ‚Üí close early.

See the difference?

The first is edge.
The second is noise.

One is repeatable.
The other bleeds you out over time.

And yeah, we all take the odd sh!t trade‚Ä¶ human nature.
But if you can pause and ask: ‚ÄúReal trade or just a punt?‚Äù

‚Ä¶you'll stack far more conviction plays, and that, ladies and gents, is where the consistency lives.

  • Traders Mastermind |

Trading can feel stupidly overwhelming.

‚ÄúForget trends, reversals are best.‚Äù
‚ÄúI just scalp.‚Äù

Theoretical setups flop when tested.

COMMIT

Run a 90-day sprint in one direction.

Not dabbling. Not tinkering. Not ‚Äútrying a bit of this, bit of that.‚Äù

Pick one playbook. Immerse yourself. Block everything else out.

Why 90 days?

  • üëâ Entrepreneurs use it for goal cycles.
  • üëâ Athletes call it a mesocycle, focus on one skill for 12 weeks.
  • üëâ UFC fighters build 12-week camps.

It works.

90 days is long enough to see results‚Ä¶ short enough to keep urgency.

And at the end, you'll know:

  • ✅ ‚ÄúThis is working, I'm keeping the momentum.‚Äù
  • ❌ ‚ÄúThis path is BS, I'm switching lanes.‚Äù

Real progress comes like the ocean eroding rock‚Ä¶ invisible day to day, inevitable over time.

üò°Can't stop blowing up accounts

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |

Welcome to Wednesday.

Now, you might think Nvidia is the biggest thing today‚Ä¶ but nope.

The real headline? This email. ü§î

Anyway‚Ä¶ a trader asked me:

‚ÄúI keep blowing up accounts after good runs, and the psychology is killing me.‚Äù

Common problem. It's the old trader saying amplified:

‚ÄúEat like a bird, sh*t like an elephant.‚Äù

Make steady progress, then torch it with one or two bad trades/days.

So, how do you fix it?

FIND YOUR DECISION POINT

The first step: figure out why.

You're not blowing up because your strategy has a normal drawdown.

You're blowing up because of too much size, too many trades, and the desperation to ‚Äúget it back.‚Äù

But here's the thing:

There's always a decision point.

That moment on your equity curve where something flips in your brain.

Where you stop trading like you did on the way up‚Ä¶ and start trading not to lose.

Your job is to find it.

Pull up the equity curves of every blown account.

Spot the inflection point.

Then go back through the blotter and look at the trades around it.

Chances are, the catalysts are the same every time:

  • üëâ A string of losers.
  • üëâ Forced trades in chop.
  • üëâ A tilt moment after missing a move.

But when you're in the heat of it, the emotion blinds you to the pattern.

Identify the decision point ‚Üí and you've already won half the battle.

Then you can actually build the fix‚Ä¶ and instead of blowing up, push the account back to highs‚Ä¶

Thursday, August 28, 2025

China sales doubt blurs Nvidia beat

  • Morning Bid U.S. |
  • morningbid@thomsonreuters.com |
  • 13:30
hr

Dollar drop on politicized Fed may be part of Trump deal

The world needs to brace itself. U.S. dollar losses on an unraveling of Federal Reserve independence may not simply be the fallout, it's likely the intention.

Donald Trump's daily bashing of the U.S. central bank this year has left little doubt that he intends to exert greater political influence over the Fed than any president since the 1970s.

His legally contentious move to fire Lisa Cook from the Fed board over allegations of mortgage fraud - based on loans taken out before she even joined the Fed - has been read by most people as a pretty clear attempt to create another vacancy on a seven-person board where members have long 14-year tenures.

If successful in dismissing Cook, Trump would secure a majority of apparent loyalists on the board next year - two are already in place, another position is in the process of being filled by his economics advisor Stephen Miran, and then there's the replacement for brow-beaten Chair Jerome Powell, whose seat is up for grabs in May.

Not only is Trump filling the board with like-thinking economists, but there are reports he is also seeking ways to shape the re-appointment of regional Fed bosses who make up the rest of the monetary policymaking council. These 12 Fed Presidents serve rolling five-year terms but all 12 come up for reappointment in February and the Fed board needs to approve them.

What does Trump want to do with the Fed? One of the president's publicly stated aims is getting interest rates down more than three percentage points to 1% - a move that would likely have a pretty dramatic downward impact on the dollar if even halfway successful.

But it's widely accepted the administration wants what it sees as a still over-valued dollar to depreciate further to help rein in U.S. deficits and reinvigorate U.S. industry - something Miran has written about extensively and Trump has publicly sympathized with.

It's likely a feature rather than a bug of its re-politicizing of the central bank.

XTX Markets

On their site they put it like this:

‚ÄúWe are a leading algorithmic trading firm that uses state-of-the-art machine learning technology to produce price forecasts for over 50,000 financial instruments across equities, fixed income, currencies, commodities, and crypto."

Source - XTXMarkets

And being the market nerd I am, I wanted to know:

What does an actual trade look like?

(Because, spoiler alert: it ain't no bull flag on the 1-min Nasdaq üòé)

Turns out their signals are probably a lot about the order book:

  • üìä Imbalances ‚Äî bids vs offers at each level
  • ‚ö° Quote dynamics ‚Äî how often prices update
  • üíß Liquidity shifts ‚Äî size pulled just before a move
  • üî• Sweep patterns ‚Äî aggressive trades hitting multiple levels (aka momentum ignition I guess)

Then add tick-by-tick patterns like:

  • ‚û° Micro-momentum (eg. 5 buy sweeps in a row)
  • ‚û° Reversion signatures (‚Äúlast sweep was overdone, odds of bounce = x%‚Äù)
  • ‚û° Intraday seasonality (NY open, close, liquidity pockets)

All of that goes into their 25,000 Nvidia AI chips, chewed up in a data centre, and spat out as trades‚Ä¶ filled before you or I even open a ticket.

(Bet they made a killing over NVDA earnings yesterday!)

Rethinking Stops üö¶

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:01

Let's talk stop losses‚Ä¶ (hey, no yawning at the back üòÖ)

The textbook says: ‚ÄúSet your stop and forget it.‚Äù

Buy at 100, stop at 90. Simple.

And for many traders, that's fine, clean, mechanical, done.

But risk doesn't always need to be managed the textbook way‚Ä¶

STOPS FRAMED DIFFERENTLY

In my latest podcast episode, I dig into alternative ways to think about stops.

And yeah, I know I do bang on about this‚Ä¶

But, I see it all the time: traders taking the standard advice, applying it to every setup‚Ä¶ and wondering why it fails.

Sure, if a trade is invalid at a clean level, that's your stop. Easy. ‚úÖ

But if your only reason for placing a stop is ‚ÄúI just don't want to lose more‚Äù‚Ä¶ that might not be the best approach.

Sometimes the smarter move is saying:

‚ÄúI'm willing to give this a bit more room, because the odds are in my favour.‚Äù

That's the point.

Stops aren't just damage control.

They can be tools to frame risk differently‚Ä¶ and that shift can open up new ways to build edge.

The set-up going into September

From that standpoint, life for risk bulls is sweet and really since the April lows, risk markets have been exceptionally kind to those who stayed the course and added risk even on shallow pullbacks.

Event Risks to Navigate in the Week Ahead

US: Labour market in focus with JOLTS (job openings, layoffs, quits rate), weekly jobless claims, and nonfarm payrolls (NFP). Also, ISM manufacturing and services surveys (both expected to improve). Fed speakers include Musalem, Williams, and Goolsbee ‚Äî the latter two speak after the payrolls report, so markets will be watching closely for any shifts in their guidance.

Outside the US: Canadian employment data, EU & Swiss CPI, Australian Q2 GDP, and UK PMIs. The US NFP report on Friday is the pivotal release. At Jackson Hole, Jay Powell made clear his concern about a cooling labour market. If payrolls are the Fed's focus, options dealers should price higher implied volatility across S&P 500 and cross-asset options going into the event.

The markets current base case: The median estimate from economists is +75k jobs, and the U/E rate eyed to tick up to 4.3%. If this outcome is realised, the Fed should cut 25bp in September ‚Äî an outcome already implied with 88% probability by interest rate swaps.

Stronger than expected: >150k payrolls, U/E steady at 4.2%. Fed cut odds priced into swaps should fall to an implied 60-70%, USD rallies, gold trades lower, equities rally modestly as good data is good news for risk.

The sweet spot for risk: 80k-120k payrolls, U/E at 4.2-4.3%. This would be cool enough to still justify an insurance rate cut in September, but not weak enough to stoke fears the Fed is behind the curve.

Weaker than expected: less than 50k payrolls, downward revisions, U/E at 4.4%. Swaps may price some chance of a 50bp cut, but equity markets would likely treat this as ‚Äúbad news is bad news,‚Äù with labour concerns sparking broader risk-off moves.

Win rate vs Profit: Which would you choose?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:02

Win rate is sexy.

Everyone loves to win trades.

Just look at YouTube:

  • ‚Äú99% win rate trader‚Äù
  • ‚ÄúNever had a losing day‚Äù

Why? Because humans love to win.

And I like a winning trade as much as the next guy.

I bet you do too.

Here's a quick test‚Ä¶

WIN RATE

Look at these two trading systems:

  • üëâ System One:

    Makes ¬£100k per quarter.

    Win rate = 5%.

    That's 19 losers out of 20; strings of 50+ losses are common, but the few winners cover it all.

  • üëâ System Two:

    Makes ¬£95k per quarter.

    Win rate = 98%.

    You win 49 out of 50 trades. Almost every trade is green.

Which one do you take?

Most traders pick System Two.

Even though it makes ¬£5k less.

Why? Because the ride feels smoother.

And that's the thing.

Losing streaks hurt. They chip away at confidence. You doubt the system. You meddle with size, stops, triggers.

You feel like you're doing the right thing, but often make it worse.

A lower win rate can be tough on the mind.

A high win rate? Dopamine on tap!

Smooth equity curve. Easy to keep going.

And real-world trading isn't always about the spreadsheet.

Someone who's never traded will never get why you'd ‚Äúchoose‚Äù to make less money.

But if it keeps you executing well? It's worth it.

Optimal on paper doesn't always equal optimal in practice.

So before you say:

‚ÄúI'll hold longer‚Ä¶ make more‚Ä¶ even if my win rate drops‚Ä¶‚Äù

Remember, it's always a trade-off.

There's a middle ground.

Yes, P&L matters most‚Ä¶ but there's a point where the extra stress just isn't worth the extra cash.

Since 2010, the choice of experienced traders.

Should You Tell People You're a Trader?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:03

No webinar today - New theme starts next week.

Here's a fun one‚Ä¶

Should you tell people you are a trader?

After 24 years in the game, my answer: it depends.

SOOOO‚Ä¶. WHAT DO YOU DO?

In some circles, you'd get a warmer reception admitting you're a bank robber‚Ä¶

You're instantly the villain who ‚Äúcaused the financial crisis,‚Äù ‚Ä¶a heartless wan*ker in a Porsche, (aka Jerk for my non-Brit friends) ‚Ä¶plucking pennies from pensioners and laughing all the way to your offshore account.

In other circles, though? You'll get a genuine chat about the economy, markets, and even someone telling you their uncle made a killing on Bitcoin. (Side note: did every uncle make a killing on Bitcoin? üòÅ)

So, just like reading the chart‚Ä¶ you've got to read the room.

If someone asks what you do, don't immediately hit them with ‚ÄúI'm a trader.‚Äù That's like going all-in on the first ignition candle.

Instead, put out a little feeler position first: ‚ÄúOh, I'm involved with the financial markets‚Ä¶ how about you?‚Äù

Nine times out of ten, they'll just start waffling about their own job. Great. Bullet dodged.

But if they probe further, that's when you've got to read the tape:

  • If they hit you with: ‚ÄúI tried Forex once‚Ä¶ it's rigged!‚Äù

    ‚Äãüö® Exit immediately. No liquidity there.

  • If they say: ‚ÄúTrading? That's just gambling!‚Äù

    üö® Fade the move, no edge in that conversation.

  • If they smirk: ‚ÄúWell, if you're so good, why aren't you richer than Jeff Bezos?‚Äù

    ‚Äãüö® Maximum stop-out. Abort.

Truth is, I don't love talking trading with non-traders anyway.

We both know how hard it is to explain. I'd rather talk markets with a real trader like you than some stranger at a BBQ.

But once in a while? You'll find someone who's genuinely curious. That's a high-quality setup.

And here's the thing: if you're still a ‚Äúdeveloping‚Äù trader, those moments often make you realise just how much you actually know‚Ä¶

You've got more edge in your back pocket than you think.

Wednesday, September 3, 2025

What was Jesse Livermore's actual trading strategy?

  • Traders Mastermind |
  • markh@tradersmastermind.com |
  • 13:03

Well‚Ä¶ wasn't yesterday a wild ride on the US indices?

Starting September as it means to go on perhaps ü§î

So, it's been a while since we visited our old pal Jesse Livermore.

We've done his quotes. We've done his life.

But here's the real question:

‚Äãüëâüèª What was his actual trading strategy?

JESSE LIVERMORE'S PLAYBOOK

Now, neither Reminiscences of a Stock Operator nor How to Trade in Stocks lays it out in clean, step-by-step detail.

Partly because back then he couldn't exactly say: ‚ÄúBuy when RSI crosses up through the Bollinger Band crush. Here's a chart‚Ä¶‚Äù

And partly because I think his style evolved over time.

Still‚Ä¶ if you piece it together, a pattern emerges.

Let's see what we can find‚Ä¶

  • üìç Trade Only at Pivotal Points

    He didn't guess bottoms or chase every breakout.

    He waited for what he called a ‚Äúpivotal point‚Äù... that psychological moment where price had to show its hand.

    Think a Wyckoff spring or a breakout that 'shouldn't' have happened‚Ä¶ but did.

    ‚ÄúWhen a speculator can determine the Pivotal Point of a stock and interpret the action at that point, he may make a commitment with the positive assurance of being right from the start.‚Äù

  • ü•á Follow the Leaders

    Livermore didn't waste time scanning hundreds of charts.

    He focused on the market leaders‚Ä¶ the strongest stocks in the strongest sectors.

    Why? Because he thought they telegraphed what the whole market wants to do.

    ‚ÄúConfine your studies of movements to the prominent stocks of the day.‚Äù

  • ‚Äãüìà Ride It. Add to It. Sit on It.

    Once in, he'd let time do its thing, adding only when he was right.

    Never averaging down.

    Letting the big swing play out.

    ‚ÄúThe big money is made in the big swing.‚Äù

    ‚ÄúIt was never my thinking that made the big money ‚Äî it was my sitting.‚Äù

    ‚ÄúI never average down. I add only when I'm right.‚Äù

  • ‚õî Exit on Abnormal Behaviour

    Just as he waited for ‚Äúnormal‚Äù pivotal action to enter, it seems he watched for what he called ‚Äúabnormal‚Äù behaviour to exit.

    Things like:

    • Failed follow-through
    • Loss of momentum
    • Time decay
    • Price not acting in line with his thesis

    When the rhythm of a strong move broke‚Ä¶he closed.

  • üß† Track, Reflect, Control

    Above all, he knew the battle wasn't just in the tape.

    It was in himself, and he kept detailed trading journals.

    ‚ÄúMy records began to talk to me.‚Äù

    ‚ÄúThe market didn't beat me. I beat myself.‚Äù

So, that's Jesse Livermore's trading strategy in a nutshell.

Not a rigid system. Not a holy grail.

A framework built on reading price at the right moments, riding leaders, and managing himself as much as the trade.

PS: Fun fact‚Ä¶ Did you know Jesse Livermore's great-granddaughter was a p*rn star?!

Yeah‚Ä¶ I'll let you search that one üëÄ

Do nothing for 15 mins or shock yourself?

This might seem off-piste‚Ä¶ but stick with me, the trading link will become obvious.

Humans HATE being bored.

In a Harvard experiment, people were asked to sit in a room for 6-15 minutes with nothing to do but think.

Many found it so unbearable‚Ä¶ they preferred to give themselves electric shocks rather than sit quietly.

Yep. Actual f*cking shocks. ‚ö°Ô∏èüôÑ

BOREDOM

Turns out our brains are hardwired to escape boredom.

In daily life, you grab your phone.

But that's weakness disguised as a solution‚Ä¶ a habit that kills focus when you need it most.

Every scroll hardwires the wrong neurons.

So when you're at the desk, that ‚Äúitch‚Äù shows up as:

  • üëâ A cheeky scalp
  • üëâ A forced entry
  • üëâ A meddled trade

All just to make the boredom go away.

And nine times out of ten?

It costs you...

The real edge is learning to be OK with boredom. To sit. To wait. To hold.

Harvard Professor Arthur Brooks nails this in a brilliant short video. Why boredom is essential, and how to train your brain not to sabotage itself.

If you're an over-trader, a meddler, or just a boredom trader, this might be the best 6 minutes you'll ever spend:

You Need to Be Bored. Here's Why.

Bonds bounce, tech rallies

  • Morning Bid U.S. |
  • morningbid@thomsonreuters.com |
  • 13:41

'Fed put' works for stocks but not long bonds

The epicenter of market anxiety right now is spiking long-term government borrowing rates, and rescuing that market will be far more complicated than steadying an equities wobble.

Tighter monetary and fiscal policy would typically be the solution to worries about aggravated inflation and mounting public debt, but that prescription can also depress growth and potentially exaggerate a tax revenue problem.

Deftness is required. What's not required is easy money.

For decades, equity investors have talked about the so-called central bank "put" - options market parlance for a policy safety net that limits sharp stock losses with restorative interest rate cuts and liquidity injections.

Popularized during the tenure of former Federal Reserve Chair Alan Greenspan in the 1990s, the "Fed put" essentially worked as advertised. Authorities could justify easing policy with the need to tamp down excess volatility and business uncertainty or the argument that the "negative wealth effect" could harm the wider economy.

Many economists and market observers worried back then that encouraging this belief would encourage undue risk-taking, which largely proved correct in the lead-up to the 2007-2008 banking crash and global recession.

But central banks' decade-long response to that credit shock took the form of balance sheet expansion and money printing, resuscitating the idea that a policy put existed.

Not only have these actions skewed markets by essentially making Wall Street equities "risk-free" over the past decade, including during the COVID-19 pandemic, but they have also allowed the U.S. government - like many of its peers - to stack up ever more debt, not least because the central bank has been hoovering up many of the bonds.

One glance at the performance of long-term government bonds this year - and particularly this week - suggests markets are calling time on that debt buildup.

If so, perhaps it's time to activate the central bank put to keep debt affordable and governments solvent?

Not so fast, and not so easy.

NO IFS OR PUTS

Rising debt is only part of the problem. If it was the only issue, then lower policy rates might well work to resolve debt sustainability math.

The real worry is that unlike during much of the past two decades, we may now be approaching a "crisis" the Fed can't easily resolve.

So back in August 2000, top trader Linda Raschke did an interview with Active Trader Magazine.

(Don't bother Googling them.. the old URL now redirects to some dodgy casino site. I'll drop the proper PDF link below üëá)

And unlike the ‚ÄúI made bank from trendline breaks while sitting by the pool‚Äù interviews we're bombarded with these days‚Ä¶

üëâ This one was real insight.

How a pro actually thinks. How she actually trades.

And yeah, it was 25 years ago‚Ä¶ but as Jesse Livermore reminded us:

‚ÄúThere is nothing new on Wall Street‚Ä¶ Whatever happens in the stock market today has happened before and will happen again. This is because human nature does not change.‚Äù

So here are some timeless takeaways

LINDA'S BIG LESSONS

  • #1 Systems = Forecasting Value

    Linda built trading models, but didn't trade them blindly.

    She used signals for bias.

    If her model was long S&P, she'd align her scalps with the long side‚Ä¶ not just buy because the system said so.

  • #2 ‚ÄúLength of Line‚Äù Filter

    Measure the total distance price travels in a session.

    Up 200, down 100, up 300, down 300 = 900 points.

    The bigger the ‚Äúline,‚Äù the better the intraday opportunity.

  • #3 Hold Time + Scaling

    Her intraday hold time? About 10 minutes.

    And she'd often scale.

    Taking half off at target if unsure about follow-through.

  • #4 The TICK Index

    She loved it. (Me too! Check my TICK Index webinar if you missed it.)

    Short Term Trading Strategies - Using The TICK Index: A Day Trader's Quick Guide

  • #5 Keep It Simple

    Wyckoff springs. Upthrusts. Bull & bear flags.

    You don't need 100 patterns.

    Just learn a few and master them.

Great stuff, Linda, really great stuff.

What a week‚Ä¶

Beautiful condition, shipped from some guy in the US.

And one passage really struck me.

PICK A DIRECTION

Turns out, a lot of the legendary old-school traders were all saying the same thing:

  • Wyckoff: ‚ÄúThe mind is not clear when the trader is working both sides of the market.‚Äù
  • Taylor: ‚ÄúThe trader should align with the day's intent, buy on Buy Days, sell on Sell Days. Don't fight the rhythm.‚Äù
  • Crabel: ‚ÄúFiltering for direction increases the odds of success. Most patterns work better when aligned with the dominant trend or bias.‚Äù

Different eras. Different markets. Same lesson.

Even if you think you're good enough to trade both directions at once‚Ä¶ ‚Ä¶maybe you're better off sticking with just one. ü§∑üèº‚Äç‚ôÇÔ∏è

That's the topic of this week's podcast episode.
